# Knit Note — KMP Knitting App

## About This Project

**Knit Note** is a Kotlin Multiplatform (KMP) mobile app for knitters. It helps users manage knitting patterns (charts), track progress on projects, and share patterns/progress with others.

- **Platforms**: Android (Jetpack Compose), iOS (SwiftUI), macOS (SwiftUI, stretch goal)
- **Architecture**: KMP shared logic + platform-native UI
- **Data Strategy**: Local-first with cloud sync (Firebase or Supabase — to be decided via ADR)
- **Language**: Kotlin (shared), Kotlin (Android UI), Swift (iOS/macOS UI)

Created from the [ECC Base Template](https://github.com/b150005/ecc-base-template).

## Project Structure

```
knit-note/
├── shared/                    # KMP shared module
│   ├── src/commonMain/        # Shared business logic, models, repositories
│   ├── src/commonTest/        # Shared tests
│   ├── src/androidMain/       # Android-specific implementations
│   └── src/iosMain/           # iOS-specific implementations (Kotlin)
├── androidApp/                # Android application (Jetpack Compose UI)
├── iosApp/                    # iOS/macOS application (SwiftUI, Xcode project)
├── docs/
│   ├── en/                    # English documentation (source of truth)
│   └── ja/                    # Japanese translations
└── .claude/                   # Agent team and Claude Code configuration
```

## Architecture Principles

- **Clean Architecture** with clear separation: UI → ViewModel → UseCase → Repository → DataSource
- **KMP shared module** contains: domain models, use cases, repository interfaces, and common utilities
- **Platform-native UI**: Android uses Jetpack Compose, iOS/macOS uses SwiftUI + UIKit (via `UIViewControllerRepresentable`/`UIViewRepresentable` where SwiftUI alone is insufficient)
- **Repository pattern** for data access abstraction (local DB + remote sync)
- **Immutable data structures**: use Kotlin `data class` with `copy()`, Swift structs
- **Dependency injection**: Koin for shared/Android, native DI patterns for iOS
- **Unidirectional data flow**: State flows down, events flow up

## Key Technology Stack

| Layer | Technology |
|-------|-----------|
| Shared Logic | Kotlin Multiplatform |
| Android UI | Jetpack Compose + Material 3 |
| iOS/macOS UI | SwiftUI + UIKit (interop as needed) |
| Local Database | SQLDelight (multiplatform) |
| Networking | Ktor Client (multiplatform) |
| Serialization | kotlinx.serialization |
| Async | Kotlin Coroutines + Flow (shared), Swift async/await (iOS) |
| DI | Koin Multiplatform |
| Image Loading | Coil (Android), platform-native (iOS) |
| Build System | Gradle (KMP), Xcode via XcodeGen (iOS) |

## Domain Model (Core Concepts)

- **Pattern**: A knitting chart/pattern with metadata (name, difficulty, gauge, yarn info, chart image/data)
- **Project**: An instance of working on a pattern (start date, current row/round, status)
- **Progress**: Row-by-row or section-based progress tracking with timestamps
- **Share**: Exported pattern or progress snapshot for sharing with others

## Agent Team

This project uses an agent team for structured development. The **orchestrator** agent coordinates the following specialists:

| Agent | Role |
|-------|------|
| orchestrator | Analyzes issues, creates plans, delegates to specialists |
| product-manager | Product planning, PRD, user stories, acceptance criteria |
| market-analyst | Market research, competitor analysis |
| monetization-strategist | Business model, pricing, revenue strategy |
| ui-ux-designer | UI/UX design, accessibility, usability review |
| docs-researcher | Documentation research, API verification, freshness-safe search |
| architect | System architecture, technology decisions |
| implementer | Code implementation following architecture and TDD |
| code-reviewer | Code quality and standards review |
| test-runner | Test execution, coverage reporting |
| linter | Static analysis, code style enforcement |
| security-reviewer | Vulnerability detection, OWASP Top 10 |
| performance-engineer | Profiling, bottleneck identification, optimization |
| devops-engineer | CI/CD, deployment strategy, release management |
| technical-writer | Documentation, changelog, bilingual docs |
| knitter | Domain advisor on knitting symbols, bilingual labels, and craft conventions (first-pass reviewer; escalates conflicts to user) |

### Ecosystem Detection

Agents detect this project as **Kotlin Multiplatform** by finding:
- `build.gradle.kts` with KMP plugin configuration
- `shared/` module with `commonMain`, `androidMain`, `iosMain` source sets
- `androidApp/` with Jetpack Compose dependencies
- `iosApp/` with Xcode project and SwiftUI

## Development Workflow

> Branch protection, PR requirements, status check gates, and bypass mechanics are documented in [docs/en/repo-policy.md](../docs/en/repo-policy.md) (JA: [docs/ja/repo-policy.md](../docs/ja/repo-policy.md)). The active ruleset is `main-strict` (id `15581036`). The Owner has Admin-role bypass for emergency direct push; everyone else must go through PR.

1. **Issue Analysis**: Feed issues to the orchestrator via GitHub MCP or copy-paste
2. **Product Planning**: The product-manager creates PRD, user stories, and acceptance criteria
3. **Research & Reuse**: Search GitHub, package registries, and docs before writing new code
4. **Architecture**: The architect designs the solution; significant decisions are recorded as ADRs in `docs/en/adr/`
5. **Implementation**: The implementer writes code following TDD (RED -> GREEN -> IMPROVE)
   - Shared logic in `shared/src/commonMain/`
   - Android UI in `androidApp/`
   - iOS UI in `iosApp/`
6. **Quality Gate**: The code-reviewer, linter, security-reviewer, and performance-engineer validate the implementation
   - After task completion, request a code review from the code-reviewer agent
   - Fix ALL reported issues (CRITICAL, HIGH, MEDIUM, and LOW)
   - Re-run the code review after fixes
   - Repeat the review-fix cycle until no issues remain (APPROVED)
   - Only then proceed to commit
7. **Documentation**: The technical-writer updates docs and changelog
8. **Release**: The devops-engineer manages deployment and release
9. **Commit, Push & CI Verification**: When the code review is APPROVED and all tests pass:
   - **Pre-commit CI check**: If any CI workflow file (`.github/workflows/`) was modified, reproduce its build/test commands locally before committing to catch task name mismatches, missing dependencies, or configuration errors early
   - **Pre-commit CI warning check**: After pushing, review CI logs for warnings (not just failures). Warnings such as deprecated actions, missing configuration fields, or fallback behaviors indicate latent issues that should be fixed proactively
   - Commit using conventional commits format (feat, fix, refactor, docs, test, chore, perf, ci)
   - Push to `origin/main`
   - **Temporary CI-wait policy (in effect from 2026-04-22, revisit when the i18n screen sweep + Phase 32.x settle)**: do **NOT** block the session waiting for CI / Security / E2E to turn green. Push and proceed directly to the next task. Rationale: each commit triggers ~30 min of remote CI, and blocking on three parallel runs per commit burns development throughput while the pre-push invariants (`ktlintCheck`, `compileTestKotlinIosSimulatorArm64`, `testAndroidHostTest`, `koverVerify`, `verifyI18nKeys`) are reliably catching regressions locally. If a prior commit's CI went red, the user surfaces it at the start of the next session as part of the handoff restate. Pre-commit CI-file reproduction and the post-push warning scan above still apply on commits that touch `.github/workflows/` — the only change is "skip the blocking CI wait".
   - These steps are performed autonomously — no user confirmation needed
10. **Next Step Planning**: At each task boundary (phase completion, milestone), convene the agent team (architect, product-manager, implementer, etc.) to discuss and agree on the next priority. Output the result as Next Session Instructions for handoff.
    - **Default to agent-team deliberation for ALL project decisions** — path choice, scope questions, prioritization, tradeoff calls. Never present a single-voice recommendation as the default when multiple reasonable paths exist. Concise roleplayed voices (product-manager, architect, implementer, knitter, ui-ux-designer as relevant; 2–3 sentences each) in a single response are acceptable for path-choice decisions; spawn real sub-agents only when the question needs deep investigation (codebase exploration, security review, etc.). End every team deliberation with an explicit **Decision:** line so the user sees the conclusion, not just the debate.
    - **Ignore implementation cost in path choices**: AI agents do the implementation, so effort/time is not a scarce resource from the user's perspective. Never cite "hours", "fits in this session", "quick win", "low-cost", or any time-estimate framing as a reason to prefer one path over another. Compare paths on user value, strategic leverage, risk, and information-gathering value only. If a path has genuinely larger scope, name the scope ("requires X new screens" / "touches Y subsystems") without a time estimate. Let the user weigh scope against value; don't pre-collapse the tradeoff by biasing toward short-horizon work. **Always pick the best outcome, not the cheapest path.**

## CI Known Limitations

- **CodeQL java-kotlin**: As of 2026-04-27, CodeQL CLI 2.25.2 (released Apr 15, 2026) supports Kotlin up to 2.3.20, so the original Kotlin-version block has resolved upstream. The `security.yml` job still fails with `continue-on-error: true`, but the actual error has shifted to `CodeQL detected code written in Java/Kotlin but this run didn't build any of it, or CodeQL could not process any of it` — the Kotlin extractor is no longer hooking into the Gradle in-process compilation, despite `--no-daemon` + `-Pkotlin.daemon.enabled=false` + `-Dkotlin.compiler.execution.strategy=in-process` flags being passed. Root cause not yet diagnosed; possibly an interaction between AGP 9.x KMP plugin's compileAndroidMain task graph and CodeQL extraction hooks. The `continue-on-error` keeps CI green while this is investigated. Reproduced identically on both `ubuntu-latest` GitHub-hosted runner and self-hosted Mac runner — not runner-specific. Required-status-checks excludes this matrix entry. The overlay-base database warning (`build-mode is set to "manual" instead of "none"`) is benign — CodeQL falls back to full (non-incremental) analysis.
- **Maestro + iOS 26**: Maestro 2.4.0 cannot reliably tap SwiftUI `Button` elements inside `List` sections on iOS 26 — the first tap works but subsequent taps are silently dropped. Also, `inputText` into `.searchable` does not update the SwiftUI `@State` binding. Affected iOS E2E flows are tagged `skip-ios26` and excluded from `run-ios.sh`. Both issues are upstream Maestro/XCTest compatibility bugs that resolve when Maestro ships iOS 26 support.
- **Maestro + SwiftUI Button on headless CI**: Maestro `tapOn` (both text and accessibility ID) does not reliably register SwiftUI `Button` taps on headless CI simulators (macOS GitHub Actions runner). The iOS onboarding helper bypasses this by relaunching the app with `-has_seen_onboarding true` launch argument, which NSUserDefaults picks up from the argument domain.
- **E2E local-only mode**: CI builds use empty Supabase credentials (local-only mode). Flows that require a live Supabase backend (e.g., Discovery browse) are tagged `requires-supabase` and excluded from CI. Run these flows locally against a Supabase-connected build.
- **iOS NavigationStack edge-swipe**: iOS 16+ `NavigationStack` does not expose a public API to disable the left-edge swipe-to-pop gesture while keeping the rest of the bar interactive. `.interactiveDismissDisabled` applies only to modally presented sheets, not pushed stack entries. Screens with discard-guard semantics (e.g. the structured chart editor) hide and replace the default back button so tapping it routes through a confirmation dialog, but the edge-swipe still pops silently. Disabling the gesture requires dropping to UIKit (`navigationController.interactivePopGestureRecognizer.delegate = self`), which is out of scope for the shared-module architecture. Users on iOS who care about in-flight edits should use the top-bar back button.
- **CMP resources on AGP 9.x KMP library plugin**: The `com.android.kotlin.multiplatform.library` plugin used by `:shared` (Phase 15.5) does not wire the Compose Multiplatform resource generator into the Android assets pipeline. The `preparedResources/commonMain/composeResources/` CVR files never get copied into `assembledResources/androidMain/`, so the final APK contains zero `composeResources/` entries and any `stringResource(Res.string.*)` throws `MissingResourceException` at runtime. Worked around in `androidApp/build.gradle.kts` via a `CopyComposeResourcesForAndroid` task wired through `androidComponents.onVariants { variant.sources.assets?.addGeneratedSourceDirectory(...) }` — resolves to `assets/composeResources/<package>/values*/*.cvr` in the APK. Remove the workaround when upstream JetBrains integration lands for this plugin. Note: Phase 33.1 shipped with this crash latent (ChartEditorScreen is never opened in E2E); Phase 33.1.1 exposed it via the SymbolGalleryScreen migration, which is exercised by `e2e/flows/android/P1_symbol_gallery.yaml`.
- **iOS XCUITest `testDeepLink_invalidURL_doesNotNavigate` simulator flake**: `DeepLinkUITests.testDeepLink_invalidURL_doesNotNavigate` has flaked once on the `macos-15-arm64` GHA runner (CI run 24885305441, commit 58395e4) with `Failed to get background assertion for target app with pid NNN: Timed out while acquiring background assertion.` This is the XCTest ⇄ SpringBoard assertion-acquisition subsystem timing out — unrelated to the app code, and reproduces as transient on cold simulators under runner contention. Does not indicate a Phase 34 regression (shared + Android jobs green on the same commit). Re-run of the same workflow would almost certainly pass. If the flake becomes chronic, the two interventions are: (1) add a retry wrapper around the XCUITest invocation at the workflow level, or (2) add `CocoaLumberjack`-style debug logging to `AppRootView` to observe the foreground-activation lifecycle the assertion acquisition is gating on. Until either trigger fires, we document and tolerate.

## Testing Requirements

- Minimum 80% test coverage for shared module
- **Unit tests** (commonTest): Domain models, use cases, repository logic
- **Android tests**: Compose UI tests, ViewModel tests
- **iOS tests**: XCTest for SwiftUI views and ViewModels
- **Integration tests**: SQLDelight database operations, Ktor API calls
- **E2E tests**: Critical user flows (create pattern, track progress, share)

### Testing Tools

| Platform | Framework |
|----------|-----------|
| Shared (commonTest) | kotlin.test |
| Android | JUnit 5, Compose UI Testing, Turbine (Flow testing) |
| iOS | XCTest, Swift Testing |
| E2E | Maestro (YAML flows, `e2e/` directory) |

## Code Quality Standards

- Functions: < 50 lines
- Files: 200-400 lines typical, 800 max
- Validate all inputs at system boundaries
- Handle errors explicitly at every level
- Never hardcode secrets; use environment variables or BuildConfig/Info.plist
- Use `ktlint` for Kotlin formatting
- Use `SwiftFormat` / `SwiftLint` for Swift formatting
- Gradle: use version catalogs (`libs.versions.toml`)

## Documentation Convention

- Technology reference docs: `docs/en/` (English, source of truth)
- Japanese translations: `docs/ja/` (maintained translations)
- Claude reads `docs/en/` only to minimize context window usage
- Japanese files include a header linking to the English source
- ADRs in `docs/en/adr/` and `docs/ja/adr/`

## Session Handoff Protocol

Each session MUST end with a **Session Task Prompt** block output as a fenced code block in the conversation (never written to any file). This block is the prompt the user will paste back at the start of the next session to instruct you on what to do — so write it in the imperative second-person voice ("Your task this session is X", "Run Y", "Open Z"), NOT as a third-person prediction of what a future session will do. The reader of this block IS the session doing the work.

The handoff is a short tactical prompt for resuming work — NOT a comprehensive status dump. Persistent facts live in this CLAUDE.md; the handoff only carries what the resuming session needs to act immediately.

### What goes in the handoff — keep terse (target ≤40 lines)
1. **Heading**: start with a clear task-prompt header, e.g. `# Your task this session` or `## Task for this session` — NOT `## Next Session Instructions` (that phrasing makes the reader think the task belongs to someone else).
2. **Current state**: branch + latest commit hash + test count + CI status (one line each)
3. **Your task**: one-line imperative statement of the phase / option to execute ("Implement Phase 30.4 glyph bundle", not "Phase 30.4 glyph bundle is next")
4. **First actions**: 3–5 concrete commands or edits to run immediately (e.g. `gh run list ...` sanity check, path to the first file to open, the test to write first) — phrased as direct instructions
5. **Any pending execution decision blocking completion** (merge conflict, flaky test awaiting investigation, etc.)

### What does NOT go in the handoff — put in CLAUDE.md instead
- **Roadmap progress** → `## Development Roadmap > Completed`. Move each finished phase here in the same commit that ships it. Include test delta, key design points, scope cuts.
- **Scope decisions for the completed phase** → keep in the phase's Completed bullet (what was cut, why, when to revisit).
- **Tech debt and follow-ups** → `## Tech Debt Backlog`. One line per item, grouped by theme.
- **Architecture invariants, ADR references** → `## Architecture Principles` or the relevant ADR under `docs/en/adr/`.
- **Gotchas / local-CI divergence** → `## CI Known Limitations`.

If the handoff is growing past ~40 lines it means you are duplicating CLAUDE.md — move the content there and link to it by phase name only.

**Ordering**: emit the handoff as the very last message of the session, after every execution decision (push, CI verify, etc.) is resolved. Never emit it mid-session — state can change afterwards and the handoff goes stale.

**Voice check**: before emitting, re-read the block as if you were opening a fresh session and someone handed it to you. If any sentence reads as "the next session will do X" rather than "do X", rewrite it. The user copy-pastes this block verbatim as the first message of the resuming session — it must read as a direct instruction to that session, not a description of it.

- **Phase 27b**: v1 Store Submission Prep (Session 2) — 5 missing ProGuard navigation routes (Onboarding, Settings, PatternLibrary, PatternEdit, Discovery), GitHub Pages privacy policy deployment (EN/JA static HTML, pages.yml workflow), feature graphic real app icon (emoji→512px PNG), GitHub Pages enabled via API (591 shared tests)

- **Phase 27.1**: iOS ViewModel Lifecycle Fix — ScopedViewModel/ProjectDetailHolder holders pin Koin-resolved ViewModels across SwiftUI View re-inits, fixing a real-device onboarding bug where Next/Skip button taps dispatched events to orphan ViewModels while observers stayed bound to the original state flow. Migrated all 12 iOS screens + AppRootView to the holder pattern; added 2 XCTest regression cases and a Maestro `nextButton` flow. Android E2E stabilized against Pixel Launcher ANR via emulator RAM bump (4096 MB), VM heap (1024 MB), CPU pinning, cold-boot settle and dialog-dismiss loops. ADR-007 records the pivot away from v1.0 store submission. (591 shared + 21 iOS UI tests)

Knitter advisory caught and fixed pre-impl: M1 (solomon-knot closed-pill → open-loop form), m1 (bullion 3 coils → 2 to clear Phase 30.2 §3.5 density threshold at 24dp), m2 (dc-crossed-2 stem-endpoint comment so future readers don't "correct" top-bars back to pre-cross column positions), m3 (picot-6 loop x∈[0.1, 0.9] → x∈[0.05, 0.95] so widthUnits=2 stretch truly spans ~2 cells). Catalog total 35 crochet glyphs (~95% JP commercial coverage). - **Phase 34**: Per-Segment Progress — ships stitch/section granularity for todo/wip/done on the chart viewer, per ADR-010 and the Phase 34 PRD. Landed across two commits: `b5cf9cd` (data spine, ADR-010 steps 1–7) + `58395e4` (UI layer, US-1..US-4 + Realtime + Reset). **Data spine (b5cf9cd, +29 → 809 tests)**: `ProjectSegment` + `SegmentState` enum with deterministic id `seg:<projectId>:<layerId>:<x>:<y>` (ADR-010 §3 — avoids UUID round-trip and makes coalescing by id trivial); SQLDelight `ProjectSegment.sq` + `3.sqm` migration using `INSERT OR REPLACE` upsert (SQLDelight does not compile `ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE`, documented inline); `LocalProjectSegmentDataSource` + `RemoteProjectSegmentDataSource` + `ProjectSegmentRepositoryImpl`; Supabase migration 013 with `TEXT id` column (matches deterministic id), owner-only RLS (no public-read escape), and Realtime publication entry. Sync wiring: `SyncEntityType.PROJECT_SEGMENT` + `SyncExecutor` branch mapping INSERT/UPDATE both to `remote.upsert` and DELETE to the reset path; `remoteProjectSegment` ctor param added as trailing nullable default to keep existing `SyncExecutor` test call-sites untouched. 4 UseCases: `ObserveProjectSegmentsUseCase` (Flow for viewer overlay), `ToggleSegmentStateUseCase` (todo → wip → done → todo cyclic, AC-2.1..AC-2.3), `MarkSegmentDoneUseCase` (long-press → done idempotent, AC-3.1), `ResetProjectProgressUseCase` (AC-4.x; reads segment ids BEFORE bulk-delete so DELETEs can be enqueued per row for offline sync coalescing). Repository convention: plain-throw suspend returns (matching `StructuredChartRepository` / `ProgressRepository`) — ADR-010 §8 was updated from the initial Result<T> draft + §1 id column reconciled to TEXT. **UI layer (58395e4, +6 → 815 tests)**: Compose + SwiftUI overlay paint (done = filled `onSurface` @ 20%, wip = 2dp `primary` outline, UNDER the symbol glyph per AC-1.1/AC-1.2). Overlay respects `ChartLayer.visible` + `ChartViewerState.hiddenLayerIds` (AC-1.3). Polar charts paint no overlay and show an inline "ships in Phase 35" notice (AC-1.4) — `message_segment_progress_polar_deferred`. Tap → `ToggleSegmentStateUseCase` cycles todo → wip → done → todo via row-delete on done-tap (AC-2.1..AC-2.3). Long-press (≥500ms) → `MarkSegmentDoneUseCase` with platform haptic tick — Android `HapticFeedbackType.LongPress`, iOS `UIImpactFeedbackGenerator` (AC-3.1, AC-3.3). Reuses Phase 32 `GridHitTest` for screen→grid resolution with y-flip (AC-2.4). Empty-cell and invisible-layer taps no-op via shared `topmostLayerAt` helper (AC-2.5, AC-2.6). Project detail "Reset progress" destructive button + confirmation dialog gated on `hasStructuredChart && hasSegmentProgress`, reuses `ResetProjectProgressUseCase` from the data spine; offline-tolerant via existing PendingSync coalescing. `RealtimeSyncManager` gains a 4th channel `project-segments-<ownerId>` alongside projects / progress / patterns, owner-scoped per ADR-010 §6 — second-device sync (AC-6.x) wired end-to-end. Nav: `ChartViewer(patternId, projectId?)` threads project context; when `projectId == null` the viewer stays pure-pattern and the overlay stays empty without engaging the UseCase pipeline. 6 new i18n keys across all 5 sources (242 total, +6): `action_reset_progress`, `dialog_reset_progress_{title,body}`, `label_segments_completed` (parametric, pre-shipped for US-7 follow-up), `message_reset_progress_done`, `message_segment_progress_polar_deferred`. testTags / accessibilityIdentifiers per PRD: `segmentOverlay`, `resetProgressButton`, `resetProgressConfirmButton`. **Code review — 4 HIGH fixed pre-commit** (highest per-commit HIGH count in the codebase, worth the latent context): (1) Koin parameter cursor bug where `params.getOrNull<String>()` re-read `patternId` instead of `projectId`, silently breaking every tap — projectId always resolved to null, overlay engaged UseCase pipeline as pattern-only and taps no-op'd; (2) iOS `.simultaneousGesture` with an `Optional<Gesture>` ternary failing to compile because SwiftUI gesture modifier overloads don't accept Optional — restructured with in-closure `isPolar` guard so the modifier is unconditional and the guard sits inside the tap handler; (3) iOS tap hit-test ignored `.scaleEffect` + `.offset`, so zoomed/panned taps landed on wrong cells — added `toCanvasSpace` inverse transform; (4) iOS long-press + `onTapGesture` double-fire where the tap handler immediately cycled the freshly-done cell back to todo — added `longPressActive` flag with 0.3s suppression window after long-press fires. **Maestro**: P1 flows (Android + iOS) tagged `requires-supabase` — same linked-pattern gating constraint as Phase 32 editor: chart creation in local-only CI would need a pre-seeded fixture, deferred. **Scope cuts per PRD**: US-5 (resume viewport auto-pan) + US-7 (project detail "X / Y stitches (Z%)" summary) — both P1/P2, `label_segments_completed` parametric key pre-shipped so US-7 follow-up is a pure additive render (compute done-count / visible-cell-count in `ProjectDetailViewModel.state`, render under the counter on both platforms, deep-link to ChartViewer on tap). **Known latent iOS risk**: the `longPressActive` 0.3s suppression window is a heuristic that may double-fire on very fast taps; not exercised on a real simulator in the UI-session (compile-check only via `compileTestKotlinIosSimulatorArm64`). If iOS E2E surfaces the issue, the fix is to gate `handleTap` on a dispatched-to-main-actor `DispatchTime` delta rather than a timer. CI for 58395e4 not verified at session boundary per the Temporary CI-wait policy; b5cf9cd E2E ✅. Pre-push invariants all green on both commits (`ktlintCheck`, `compileTestKotlinIosSimulatorArm64`, `testAndroidHostTest` 815, `koverVerify`, `verify-i18n-keys.sh` 242).

- **Phase 33.3**: Android per-app locale enablement — unblocks both the end-user Android Settings > App Info > Language picker on Android 13+ and the ja-JP Maestro verification deferred in Phase 33.2-verify. Two-file change: (1) `androidApp/build.gradle.kts` gains `androidResources { generateLocaleConfig = true; localeFilters += listOf("en", "ja") }` inside `android { }` between `buildFeatures` and `packaging`; (2) new `androidApp/src/main/res/resources.properties` declares `unqualifiedResLocale=en-US` (AGP's `extractSupportedLocales` task requires this file adjacent to `values*/` directories — without it the build fails with "No resources.properties file found"). AGP then generates `xml/_generated_res_locale_config.xml` listing `en-US` (default) + `ja` and auto-injects `android:localeConfig="@xml/_generated_res_locale_config"` into the merged manifest. Verified post-build: `aapt2 dump xmltree androidApp-debug.apk AndroidManifest.xml` shows the attribute, and the generated config file content is correct. **Runtime verification**: installed APK, `adb shell cmd locale set-app-locales io.github.b150005.knitnote.android --locales ja-JP`, force-stop, relaunch — home screen renders `プロジェクトを検索…` / `すべて`-`進行中`-`未着手`-`完了` / `プロジェクトがまだありません` / `プロジェクトを作成` correctly (screenshot at `/tmp/ja-e2e/screens/after-fix.png`). "Knit Note" stays English per the `app_name` locale-identical convention. Previously `Activity.Configuration.getLocales()` silently fell back to en-US regardless of the per-app locale stored in `LocaleManagerService`; that resolution path now honors the per-app value. **E2E**: en-US `e2e/run-android.sh` 8/8 ✅ in 3m 31s (no regression). ja-JP `/tmp/ja-e2e/run-ja.sh` 8/8 ✅ in 3m 30s — **important interpretation caveat**: the dialog-content text selectors in `P0_create_project.yaml` / `P1_edit_project.yaml` (`tapOn: "Project Name"`, `tapOn: "Total Rows (optional)"`, `tapOn: "Create"`, `assertVisible: "New Project"`, etc.) still resolve under ja-JP because `CreateProjectDialog.kt` and `EditProjectDialog.kt` (under `shared/src/commonMain/.../ui/projectlist/` and `ui/projectdetail/`) have not been i18n'd yet — they still hardcode `Text("New Project")` / `label = { Text("Project Name") }` / etc. This is independent i18n debt, not a sign that the Phase 33.2 dialog-cross-window testTag issue is resolved. Tracked under the "Maestro `text: \"Back\"` / `text: \"Clear search\"` brittleness" Tech Debt entry's open-dialog half; the "ja-JP currently-passing" nature of those selectors is load-bearing on those two dialogs staying English-hardcoded until the dialog-half is closed. **`localeFilters` format gotcha** (worth documenting for next reader): code reviewer's LOW suggested BCP 47 tags `listOf("en-US", "ja-JP")` to match `resources.properties`'s `unqualifiedResLocale=en-US` spelling; applied it and the build failed with aapt2 `error: invalid config 'en-US' for -c option.` at `:androidApp:generateDebugLocaleConfig`. AGP's `localeFilters` uses aapt2 resource-qualifier format (`<lang>` bare, or `<lang>-r<REGION>` for region-qualified like `en-rGB`), NOT BCP 47 — these two config systems are distinct despite both sitting on the Android side. Reverted to `listOf("en", "ja")` with an inline Gradle comment documenting the format requirement and naming `"en-rGB"` as the hypothetical future region-variant spelling so the next reader doesn't repeat the experiment. Pre-push invariants all green (`ktlintCheck`, `compileTestKotlinIosSimulatorArm64`, `testAndroidHostTest` 780 tests, `koverVerify`, `verify-i18n-keys.sh` 232 keys). Code review: APPROVED with 1 LOW that was subsequently proven incorrect by the aapt2 format constraint — captured as an inline comment in the Gradle file so the experiment doesn't get re-run. No test delta — AGP locale config is infrastructure, not behavior.

- **Phase 33.2-verify**: post-push verification of the 33.2 testTag sweep. CI for 943ac55 confirmed green across all three jobs (CI, Security, E2E) — neither of the prior flake classes (Security CodeQL Swift ENOTFOUND, E2E iOS Maestro startup timeout) reappeared. Android emulator (API 37, `emulator-5554`) run via `e2e/run-android.sh` under the default en-US locale: **8/8 Maestro flows passed** in 3m 31s (9th flow `P1_discovery_browse` excluded by `--exclude-tags requires-supabase` as designed), confirming the 33.2 `text:` → `id:` pivots do not regress the existing en-US path. **Critical finding — ja-JP verification blocked on a latent prod gap**: attempting `adb shell cmd locale set-app-locales io.github.b150005.knitnote.android --locales ja-JP` + force-stop + relaunch rendered the app in English (`get-app-locales` returns `[ja-JP]` but the Activity's `Configuration.getLocales()` still resolves en-US). Root cause: `androidApp/src/main/AndroidManifest.xml` declares no `android:localeConfig` attribute and `androidApp/build.gradle.kts` has no `androidResources { generateLocaleConfig = true }`. Without one of those, Android 13+ `LocaleManagerService` stores the per-app locale but the runtime `Configuration` does not honor it — CMP's `Res.string.*` resolution (which reads `LocalConfiguration.current.locales`) falls back to the system locale, which was en-US on this emulator. `setprop persist.sys.locale ja-JP` failed (non-rooted emulator blocks the setprop) and `settings put system system_locales ja-JP,en-US` had no effect without a reboot, so the system-locale fallback path remained unavailable. This also explains retroactively why the prior session's "6/9 ja-JP fail" baseline was misleading — with per-app locale silently failing, those 6 failures could not have been Japanese-text-selector mismatches; they were likely stale-emulator or misconstructed-flow-copy artifacts from the `/tmp/ja-e2e/` scratch work that got wiped. **Consequence for the 33.2 sweep's acceptance criterion**: the non-dialog Tech Debt caveat ("dialog half remains open pending Maestro cross-window testTag resolution") is technically unverified under ja-JP, but the non-dialog pivots are all `text:` → `id:` swaps on testTags routed through `testTagsAsResourceId = true` — locale cannot regress an id-based selector that maps to a stable DOM `resource-id` string. en-US green confirms the pivot mechanics; ja-JP would be a sanity-assert, not a new-information test. **Scope decision**: the one-line `generateLocaleConfig = true` fix (plus adding `en` / `ja` to `androidResources.localeFilters` to constrain generation) is a legitimate production change — without it, users cannot switch the app to Japanese via Android's per-app language picker even if the app's Android-side `values-ja/strings.xml` and CMP `values-ja/strings.xml` ship complete translations. Bundling the fix into a ja-JP verification task would conflate infrastructure with verification, so per the task brief's "If a workaround approach is justified, that's a separate Phase 33.3" directive, the Gradle change lives in Phase 33.3. Discovery artifacts persist at `/tmp/ja-e2e/` (wrapper script + first-run log + two verification screenshots showing English rendering despite per-app locale set to ja-JP). Pre-push invariants unchanged from 33.2 (no code touched). No test delta.

These queries would have passed on English CI today and silently failed on any ja-locale simulator run. **Code review**: 0 CRITICAL / 2 HIGH / 2 MEDIUM / 1 LOW first pass. All 5 findings fixed pre-commit — HIGH1 `Group` → `ZStack` wrap (bare `Group` accessibility modifier propagation footgun), HIGH2 explicit `LocalizedStringKey("title_error")` wrap on `.alert(...)` (matches LoginScreen precedent; bare-literal overload resolution can drop to `String` and skip localization), MEDIUM1 dropped premature `state_no_profile` key (92 → 91; the ViewModel only emits "user == null" after a load failure, so both iOS and Kotlin branches reuse `state_profile_load_failed`), MEDIUM2 repositioned the error-deferral comment onto the `LaunchedEffect(state.error)` block it qualifies rather than the unrelated `profileUpdatedMessage` line above it, LOW1 added the SwiftUI literal-promotion table to the convention doc. - **Phase 33.1.3**: Project list i18n + search-field testTag — fourth shared Compose screen migrated after ChartEditorScreen (33.1), SymbolGalleryScreen (33.1.1), and ChartViewerScreen (33.1.2). `ProjectListScreen.kt` now resolves every user-visible literal via `stringResource(Res.string.*)`: TopAppBar title (reuses `app_name`), 7 IconButton contentDescriptions (Discover, Pattern Library, Symbol Dictionary, Profile, Activity Feed, Shared With Me, Settings), FAB New Project, search placeholder + clear button, 4 status FilterChips (All / In Progress / Not Started / Completed), SortOrder chip/menu labels (6 variants: `label_sort_*` + `_detail` siblings — `RECENT` intentionally reuses the single-form key in both chip and menu per in-code comment since "Recent" reads naturally as a menu entry), two empty-state variants (no-projects + no-matches), StatusChip (3 status variants), `ProjectCard` row-count text (parametric `label_rows_of_total` / `label_rows_current`), swipe-delete contentDescription (reuses `action_delete`), and `DeleteConfirmDialog` (title + parametric body + reused `action_delete` / `action_cancel`). 5-source parity now **65 keys** (+29). New `hint_` prefix introduced for input-field placeholders (`hint_search_projects`) and documented in `i18n-convention.md` (EN + JA) alongside explicit `title_*` / `label_*` role definitions that were implicit before. `SortOrder.chipLabelKey` / `menuLabelKey` extension properties switched from `String` to `StringResource` (pure getters; resolution happens at the composable call site — no composable-rules violation). Parametric strings use Android-standard `%1$d`/`%2$d`/`%1$s` format specifiers, mirrored as `%1$@` in xcstrings for SwiftUI native resolution. **Maestro**: 5 Android flows (`P0_app_launch`, `P0_row_counter`, `P0_create_project`, `P1_edit_project`, `P0_onboarding`) de-brittled by replacing 5 `"No projects yet"` + 1 `"Create Project"` + 1 `assertNotVisible: "No projects yet"` with the pre-existing locale-independent `createProjectFab` testTag landmark. iOS flows untouched (SwiftUI screens, separate literal surface). Other literal asserts (dialog titles, `ProjectDetail` content, status chips on specific cards) left for their respective screen-migration PRs; chip-filter taps (`"In Progress"` / `"Not Started"` / `"All"`) in `P1_search_filter` also left — they pass on CI's English locale and per-chip testTags would be a separate de-brittling sweep. **Known gotcha (fixed post-CI on follow-up commit b0fb3d8)**: Phase 33.1.3 initial commit `15a5ee5` changed the search placeholder from `"Search projects..."` (three ASCII dots) to `"Search projects\u2026"` (U+2026) per the i18n convention's `state_loading` ellipsis style — but Maestro's `tapOn: "text"` uses **regex** semantics, so the existing flow assertion `tapOn: "Search projects..."` was matching "Search projects" + any 3 chars, which does not match the single-char `…`. Failure surfaced only on the first live CI Android emulator run (`P1 - Search & Filter Projects` flow). Fixed by adding `Modifier.testTag("searchField")` to the `OutlinedTextField` and routing the Maestro tap through `id: "searchField"` — locale-independent and immune to future placeholder wording changes. Generalizable lesson: any shared-screen migration that introduces/changes a user-visible literal hit by a Maestro regex selector needs a testTag preflight. Code review: APPROVED with 2 LOW findings, both addressed pre-commit — (1) added `action_symbol_dictionary` key so the GridView IconButton's contentDescription no longer reuses the screen-title key `title_symbol_dictionary` (decouples action semantics from screen title; 5-source key addition); (2) in-code comment on `SortOrder.menuLabelKey` documenting RECENT's deliberate single-key reuse across chip + menu forms. Pre-push invariants all green on both commits (`ktlintCheck`, `compileTestKotlinIosSimulatorArm64`, `verify-i18n-keys.sh`, `testAndroidHostTest` 776 tests). CI + Security + E2E all ✅ on commit `b0fb3d8`. No test delta — CMP resource resolution is infrastructure, not behavior. **Scope cut**: still 13 shared Compose screens hardcoding English — see Tech Debt Backlog `i18n sweep across remaining shared screens`.

- **Phase 33.1.1**: Symbol gallery i18n + Android CMP resource packaging fix — second shared screen migrated after ChartEditorScreen. `SymbolGalleryScreen.kt` adds one new key (`title_symbol_dictionary` = "Symbol Dictionary" / "記号辞典") and reuses existing `action_back` for the nav IconButton contentDescription. SymbolCatalog domain labels (`SymbolCategory.jaLabel/enLabel`, `SymbolDefinition.*Label/*Description`) intentionally left unmigrated per Phase 33 non-goals in ADR-008. 5-source parity now 34 keys (33 → 34). Existing E2E flows `e2e/flows/{android,ios}/P1_symbol_gallery.yaml` updated to drop the locale-dependent `assertVisible: "Symbol Dictionary"` assertion and rely on the pre-existing locale-independent `symbolGalleryGrid` testTag — this is the only robust E2E pattern once UI text is i18n'd. **Key discovery**: Phase 33.1 shipped a latent Android runtime crash — `org.jetbrains.compose.resources.MissingResourceException: Missing resource with path: composeResources/<pkg>/values/strings.commonMain.cvr`. Root cause: the AGP 9.x `com.android.kotlin.multiplatform.library` plugin (adopted in Phase 15.5) does not wire the CMP resource generator into Android asset packaging, so the CVR files never reach the APK. ChartEditorScreen never exercised this path in CI (no E2E opens the editor), so the crash stayed dormant until SymbolGalleryScreen's Maestro flow opened the gallery and the app returned to the home launcher. Fixed in `androidApp/build.gradle.kts` via a `@CacheableTask`-annotated `CopyComposeResourcesForAndroid` task with `@PathSensitive(PathSensitivity.RELATIVE)` inputs, anchored to `rootProject.layout.projectDirectory` (not the module path, per code review), wired via `androidComponents.onVariants { variant.sources.assets?.addGeneratedSourceDirectory(...); variant.androidTest?.sources?.assets?.addGeneratedSourceDirectory(...) }` so both the main APK and instrumented-test APK get `assets/composeResources/<package>/values{,-ja}/*.cvr`. Documented in `CI Known Limitations` above. Code review: 2 HIGH + 2 MEDIUM + 2 LOW — HIGHs + MEDIUMs fixed pre-commit (androidTest wiring gap, raw `../shared/...` path anchored to rootProject, `@PathSensitive(RELATIVE)`, `@CacheableTask`), LOWs carried as written comments. Pre-push invariants all green (`ktlintCheck`, `compileTestKotlinIosSimulatorArm64`, `testAndroidHostTest` 776 tests, `koverVerify`, `verify-i18n-keys.sh` 34 keys). CI + Security + E2E all ✅ on commit `4402bf2`. **Scope cut**: still 15 shared Compose screens hardcoding English — see Tech Debt Backlog `i18n sweep across remaining shared screens`.

- **Phase 32**: Chart Editor MVP — tap-to-place authoring with undo/redo and save. Shared: `ChartEditorViewModel` (one-shot load via `GetStructuredChartByPatternId` — intentionally not observing so external Realtime does not stomp mid-edit; conflict resolution is Phase 37 scope), `EditHistory` (50-entry `ArrayDeque` snapshot ring buffer with overflow eviction + redo-clear on record), `GridHitTest` (screen→grid with y-flip), `ChartEditorScreen` (Scaffold + Canvas + palette), `SymbolPaletteStrip` (category chips + eraser + symbol cells), `cellScreenRect` extracted from viewer to shared `SymbolDrawing.kt`. iOS: `StructuredChartEditorScreen.swift` via `ScopedViewModel`, `PalettePathCache` ObservableObject, Closeable cancelled in `onDisappear`. Koin + NavGraph + ProjectDetail entries on both platforms. **Scope cuts (MVP)**: `CraftType.KNIT` / `ReadingConvention.KNIT_FLAT` hardcoded (picker = Phase 32.2), 8×8 default grid (picker = Phase 35), flat rect only (polar = Phase 35), Maestro E2E deferred (requires linked-pattern prerequisite — see Tech Debt Backlog), i18n hardcoded English. **Known gotcha that burnt CI**: Kotlin/Native rejects backticked test-fun names containing `(`, `)`, `,` — JVM tolerates. 3 tests renamed in fix commit (6b65df4). +30 commonTest (750 total). Code review: 2 HIGH + 4 MEDIUM + 3 LOW fixes landed before merge (iOS Closeable leak, `save()` stale snapshot, `!!` on errorMessage, vacuous test assertion, eraser icon semantics, pointerInput over-keying, iOS palette SVG parse cache, `availableCategories` memoization).

- **Phase 32.3**: Parametric symbol input per ADR-009 §7 — Phase 32 MVP wrote `symbolParameters = emptyMap()` for every placement, so `ch-space` (the only parametric glyph today) stuck rendering the literal `"n"` placeholder. 32.3 forks `placeCell`: eraser and non-parametric selections keep the immediate-commit path; parametric selections open an inline input dialog and defer commit to `ConfirmParameterInput`. Re-edit reopens the same dialog pre-populated when the user taps a parametric cell with the matching symbol selected. `PendingParameterInput` holds (`symbolId`, `x`, `y`, `slots`, `currentValues`, `isEditingExisting`) and every mutating path — `placeCell`, `undo`, `redo` — short-circuits while it is set, so nothing can rewrite `draftLayers` between dialog-open and confirm. `save()` is async but untouched by parametric state and gated by `hasUnsavedChanges`, so it cannot interleave either. Overwrite of a parametric cell with a non-parametric selection intentionally wipes `symbolParameters` — ADR-009 §5 round-trip preservation is scoped to storage, not editor mutation; called out in-code. Compose: `AlertDialog` + `OutlinedTextField` per slot, drafts keyed by `(x, y, symbolId)`. SwiftUI: `NavigationStack` + `Form` sheet driven by a local `@State var isParameterSheetPresented: Bool` (not a reactive binding — avoids a transient confirm-path race where reading back from the state flow in a `Binding.set` closure could spuriously fire `CancelParameterInput`); `.id("\(symbolId)@\(x),\(y)")` forces a fresh view per-pending so `.onAppear` reseeds cleanly. +8 commonTest (768 total). Code review: 2 HIGH + 4 MEDIUM + 3 LOW — fixed before commit (undo/redo pending-guards, sheet presented-flag decoupling, `.id()` robustness, test 33 catalog pre-condition, ktlint import hygiene, ADR §5 comment, concurrency-invariant comment block).

- **Phase 32.4**: System-back discard dialog — Phase 32 only intercepted the top-bar back button, so Android hardware / predictive-back and iOS NavigationStack back both silently popped the editor and dropped unsaved edits. New `expect/actual` helper `ui/platform/SystemBackHandler` wires `androidx.activity.compose.BackHandler` on Android and stays a no-op on iOS (shared Compose isn't rendered on iOS for the editor — SwiftUI is). `ChartEditorScreen.kt` gates the intercept on `state.hasUnsavedChanges`, so the normal clean-state pop behavior is preserved. iOS `StructuredChartEditorScreen.swift` now sets `.navigationBarBackButtonHidden(true)` + a custom `ToolbarItem(.topBarLeading)` back button that routes through a new local `attemptBack(state:)` helper (mirrors the Compose `attemptBack` closure). `androidx.activity.compose` dep added to shared `androidMain`. Kover exclusion for the new `ui.platform.*` package (Compose plumbing, JVM-untestable; logic is in `ChartEditorViewModel` tests). No new commonTest — the discard-dialog trigger is `state.hasUnsavedChanges` which is already covered. Known iOS limitation: edge-swipe-from-left still pops without the dialog (NavigationStack doesn't expose a swipe-disable API without dropping to UIKit); documented in CI Known Limitations. 768 shared tests (unchanged).

- **Phase 32.2**: Chart Editor craft/reading picker + iOS Closeable leak audit — surfaces `CraftType` + `ReadingConvention` in the editor so CROCHET authoring writes correct metadata instead of the Phase 32 KNIT default. `ChartEditorState` gains `draftCraftType` / `draftReadingConvention`; `SelectCraft` / `SelectReading` events update draft via atomic `_state.update { if (== val) return@update it; it.copy(...) }` guard. Metadata edits deliberately skip `EditHistory` (drawing-only) but still mark `hasUnsavedChanges` on existing charts. On a new chart, metadata alone does not mark dirty — cells are still required to save (21b/21c symmetric tests). `CreateStructuredChartUseCase` now accepts `craftType` + `readingConvention` params (defaults KNIT / KNIT_FLAT). Compose: TopBar overflow `MoreVert` → `DropdownMenu` with non-interactive `Text` section headers (no disabled-button a11y semantics), U+2713 check prefix. SwiftUI: `ellipsis.circle` `Menu` with nested `Picker`s. **Bundled iOS Closeable leak audit** (same anti-pattern fixed in Phase 32 `StructuredChartEditorScreen`): `PatternEditScreen`, `SharedContentScreen`, `DiscoveryScreen` now use `@State Closeable` + `close()` in `.onDisappear`; Discovery / SharedContent additionally guard against `.task { }` re-entry by closing prior subscription before reassigning. `iosApp/Info.plist` regenerated by xcodegen to align with Phase 33 i18n (`CFBundleDevelopmentRegion=en`, `CFBundleLocalizations=[en,ja]`). Code review: APPROVED after 2 HIGH + 2 MEDIUM fixes (TOCTOU guard moved inside `_state.update`, 21c test added, `.task { }` re-entry leak defense, DropdownMenu header a11y). +10 commonTest (760 total). **Gotcha**: `./gradlew ktlintCheck` must run locally before push — JVM toolchain tolerated prior multiline layout; CI ktlint required `computeUnsavedChanges(...)` to start on a new line (fix commit 739fc82).

- **Phase 37.4**: Branch picker + create / switch / restore (ADR-013 §6 §7) — fourth and final read/write slice of Phase 37 closes the entire collaboration-core MVP. Wires the data spine that 37.1 already shipped (`chart_branches` table + `LocalChartBranchDataSource` + `RemoteChartBranchDataSource` + `SyncEntityType.CHART_BRANCH` + `ensureDefaultBranch` auto-create on `create()` / `forkFor()`) into the user-facing branch model: branch picker on `ChartViewerScreen` overflow → "Switch branch" + "New branch" CTA, plus long-press → "Restore as new commit" on `ChartHistoryScreen` (closes the inert 37.2 reserved keys `action_restore_revision` / `dialog_restore_revision_{title,body}`). **Domain repo**: new `ChartBranchRepository` interface (`getByPatternIdAndName`, `getByPatternId`, `observeBranchesForPattern`, `createBranch`, `advanceTip`, `deleteBranch`) implemented by `ChartBranchRepositoryImpl` over the existing `LocalChartBranchDataSource` + `SyncManagerOperations`. `createBranch` is idempotent on `(patternId, branchName)` — reads first to suppress duplicate sync enqueue when the local INSERT-OR-IGNORE would no-op (same pattern as `ensureDefaultBranch`). `advanceTip` reads existing branch row first; if absent silently returns rather than upserting a new row from incomplete data (defensive against pre-37.4 charts that skipped the branch layer). `deleteBranch` enqueues a CHART_BRANCH DELETE — the existing `SyncExecutor.executeChartBranch` DELETE branch from 37.1 is now reachable. **Repository surface change**: `StructuredChartRepository.setTip(patternId: String, targetRevision: ChartRevision): StructuredChart?` is the new branch-switch primitive. `setTip` reads the current `chart_documents` row and rewrites it from the revision's payload INSIDE the same `writeMutex` that `update`/`create`/`forkFor` use — atomic read-then-write so a concurrent chart-editor save racing the switch cannot silently roll back the editor's commit (this was a HIGH from the first-pass code review on the original use-case-level read+write design; fixed by moving the read inside the mutex). Returns null when the pattern has no tip pointer row — caller treats as `NotFound`. `update()` also gains an `advanceCurrentBranchTip(patternId, previousRevisionId, newRevisionId)` private helper that finds every branch whose `tipRevisionId == previousRevisionId` and advances them in lock-step (defines "co-located branches all advance together" — after `createBranch` two branches share a tip; the next save advances both, matching the user's "I just branched from here" mental model). Defensive fallback: when no branch matches the prior tip, advance "main" via `advanceTip` so pre-37.4 charts that predate `ensureDefaultBranch` don't end up with a dangling `chart_documents.revision_id` not tracked by any branch row. Both `setTip` and `advanceCurrentBranchTip` are `null`-default-safe via the existing `chartRevisionRepository: ChartRevisionRepository?` + new `chartBranchRepository: ChartBranchRepository?` optional ctor params on `StructuredChartRepositoryImpl` — existing test call-sites that bypass the branch layer continue to compile unchanged. **Use cases**: 4 new factories registered in `UseCaseModule` — `GetChartBranchesUseCase` (live `observe(patternId)` Flow + paginated `invoke`), `CreateBranchUseCase` (validates name: empty after trim → Validation, "main" reserved case-insensitively → Validation, duplicate detected case-insensitively against `getByPatternId(...).any { equals(name, ignoreCase = true) }` → Validation; the DB itself stays case-sensitive so user-chosen casing renders verbatim), `SwitchBranchUseCase` (resolves branch + revision, delegates the atomic tip rewrite to `chartRepository.setTip`; surfaces `NotFound` if either lookup misses or the chart row is absent), `RestoreRevisionUseCase` (looks up the past revision + current chart, builds a new chart with the restored drawing payload + a new `revisionId` whose `parentRevisionId == current.revisionId` so restoration is a forward commit on top of tip — additive, NOT destructive; routes through the existing `update()` path which already handles append-history + tip-advance + branch-tip-advance). All 4 use cases use the project's standard `try { ... } catch (e: CancellationException) { throw e } catch (e: Exception) { e.toUseCaseError() }` envelope per the Phase 36.3 / 37.3 precedent — bare `catch (e: Exception)` would swallow `CancellationException` and silently convert a coroutine-cancelled timeout to a phantom `UseCaseError.Unknown`, which the first-pass code review flagged as HIGH. **`ChartBranchPickerViewModel`**: live branch list + `Channel<BranchSwitchedEvent>` for one-shot post-switch navigation. State derived via `combine(getBranches.observe(patternId), chartRepository.observeByPatternId(patternId))` so the "current branch" highlight tracks both branch tip moves AND chart updates landing through Realtime / sync — the picker stays correct across peer device pushes without a manual refresh. `BranchSwitchedEvent` carries `branchName: String` rather than being a `data object` — the ViewModel emits the user-supplied name from `handleSwitchBranch` so the consumer is independent of the timing race between `_branchSwitched.trySend` and the `combine` block writing the new `currentRevisionId` into `_state` (the two paths are concurrent on the same scope with no happens-before guarantee; first-pass code review flagged the original snapshot-from-state design as a MEDIUM where a fast switch would silently drop the Snackbar confirmation). **Compose UI**: new `ChartBranchPickerSheet` (`ModalBottomSheet` listing every branch alphabetically, current tip annotated with `AssistChip(label_current_branch)`, non-current rows expose a `Switch` `TextButton`, "+ New branch" CTA at the bottom opens an `AlertDialog` with `OutlinedTextField`). `ChartViewerScreen` adds `Icons.Default.AccountTree` "Switch branch" entry to the existing overflow menu next to the 37.2 "View history" item, threads `patternId` to the picker on selection, and bridges the `onBranchSwitched(branchName)` callback to a `Snackbar` via a `pendingSnackbar: String?` + `LaunchedEffect(pendingSnackbar)` pattern so the suspending `showSnackbar` doesn't block the picker callback. `ChartHistoryScreen` `RevisionRow` switches from `Modifier.clickable(role = Role.Button)` to `Modifier.combinedClickable(role = Role.Button, onClick, onLongClick)` (`@OptIn(ExperimentalFoundationApi::class)`); long-press dispatches `ChartHistoryEvent.LongPressRevision(revisionId)` which sets `state.pendingRestoreRevision`; that drives a Material 3 `AlertDialog` with `dialog_restore_revision_{title,body}` and confirm → `ChartHistoryEvent.ConfirmRestore` → `RestoreRevisionUseCase`. State extended with `pendingRestoreRevision: ChartRevision?` slot. `ChartHistoryViewModel` ctor gains an optional `restoreRevision: RestoreRevisionUseCase? = null` so 37.2 test call-sites stay compatible. **iOS mirror**: `iosApp/.../ChartBranchPickerSheet.swift` uses the established `ScopedViewModel` holder pattern. Sheet body is a `NavigationStack` + `List` with the `BranchRow` struct rendering each branch (current → `Label("Current", systemImage: "checkmark")`, non-current → `Button("Switch")` with `.buttonStyle(.bordered)`). "New branch" CTA in `.topBarTrailing` opens a nested `.sheet` with a `Form` containing a `TextField` for the branch name. `observeBranchSwitched()` collects the typed `wrapChartBranchSwitchedFlow` Closeable + reads `event.branchName` directly from the envelope (no state snapshot) before dispatching `onBranchSwitched(name)` on the main actor. `StructuredChartViewerScreen.swift` toolbar Menu gains a "Switch branch" `Button` with `arrow.triangle.branch` SF Symbol; switched-branch toast surfaces via a 2-second `.overlay(alignment: .bottom)` carrying the format-resolved `message_switched_to_branch` template (parity with Compose's Snackbar despite SwiftUI lacking a non-blocking equivalent in the codebase). `ChartHistoryScreen.swift` adds `.onLongPressGesture` to `RevisionRow` rendering + a `.confirmationDialog` driven by a `Binding<Bool>` derived from `state.pendingRestoreRevision != nil` — same parity contract as Compose. **DI**: `RepositoryModule` registers `ChartBranchRepositoryImpl` as `single<ChartBranchRepository>` and threads the new `chartBranchRepository = get()` into `StructuredChartRepositoryImpl`. `UseCaseModule` registers all 4 new factories. `ViewModelModule` registers `ChartBranchPickerViewModel` (parametric on `patternId`) and threads `restoreRevision = get()` into `ChartHistoryViewModel`. iOS bridge: `KoinHelper.kt` adds `getChartBranchPickerViewModel(patternId)` accessor + `wrapChartBranchPickerState` (StateFlow → FlowWrapper) + `wrapChartBranchSwitchedFlow` (Flow<BranchSwitchedEvent> → EventFlowWrapper). `ViewModelFactory.swift` adds the typed `chartBranchPickerViewModel(patternId:)` accessor. **i18n** — 8 new keys across all 5 sources (301 total, +8): `title_branch_picker`, `action_create_branch`, `dialog_create_branch_title`, `label_branch_name`, `label_current_branch`, `state_no_branches`, `action_switch`, `message_switched_to_branch` parametric (`Switched to %1$s` EN / `%1$sに切り替えました` JA where the JA puts the branch-name prefix per natural Japanese reading; iOS xcstrings uses `%1$@` per the SwiftUI native formatter convention). Reuses 37.2 `action_restore_revision` + `dialog_restore_revision_{title,body}` (no longer inert), plus existing `action_cancel` / `title_error` / `action_ok`. **Tests** — +14 commonTest landed (3 in `StructuredChartRepositoryImplTest`: update advances main branch tip, update advances co-located branches in lock-step, setTip rewrites tip pointer in place without history append; 1 in `GetChartBranchesUseCase`-coverage section: invoke returns Success with seeded branches; 5 in `CreateBranchUseCase`-coverage section: blank name rejected, "main" reserved case-insensitively, duplicate rejected, missing chart NotFound, happy path mints branch with tip at current chart revision; 4 in `SwitchBranchUseCase`-coverage section: unknown branch NotFound, missing tip revision NotFound, happy path materializes target revision preserving tip row id, missing chart row NotFound (covers the new `setTip` null return path); 2 in `RestoreRevisionUseCase`-coverage section: unknown revision NotFound, happy path appends new commit with restored payload + parent = old tip). Test fake `FakeChartBranchRepository` mirrors the production interface (idempotent `createBranch` semantics documented inline as unreachable from `CreateBranchUseCase` due to the validation pre-empt but kept for future repo-direct tests); `FakeStructuredChartRepository.setTip` updated to the new `(patternId, targetRevision)` signature with same atomic shape as production. `ChartViewerViewModelTest`'s inline `object : StructuredChartRepository` stub also updated. 1033 shared tests (+15 from 1018 baseline; ADR-013 §9's +10–15 target band, hit the upper bound). Test names follow the Phase 32 Kotlin/Native CI gotcha (no parens, commas, or apostrophes in backticks). **Kover exclusion**: `ChartBranchPickerSheetKt*` added to the Compose-UI exclusion list. `ChartBranchPickerViewModel` deliberately NOT excluded (testable mutation path; ViewModel-level coverage falls out of the use-case tests via `combine`). `ChartBranchRepositoryImpl` not excluded — pure delegate over the SQLDelight + sync layer, indirectly covered by `StructuredChartRepositoryImplTest`'s branch-tip-advance tests. **Code review**: 0 CRITICAL / 2 HIGH / 2 MEDIUM / 1 LOW first pass, all addressed pre-commit — HIGH1 (`CancellationException` swallowed in all 4 new use cases) fixed by adding the explicit `catch (e: CancellationException) { throw e }` ahead of the bare `Exception` catch per the Phase 36.3 / 37.3 precedent; HIGH2 (`SwitchBranchUseCase` TOCTOU between use-case-level chart read and repo-level write) fixed by changing the `setTip` contract from `setTip(chart): chart` to `setTip(patternId, targetRevision): chart?` and moving the read+write atomically inside `writeMutex.withLock`; MEDIUM1 (case-sensitive duplicate check vs case-insensitive "main" reservation creating UI inconsistency) fixed by switching `CreateBranchUseCase`'s duplicate check from `getByPatternIdAndName` to `getByPatternId(...).any { equals(trimmed, ignoreCase = true) }`; MEDIUM2 (`BranchSwitchedEvent` snapshot race between `_branchSwitched.trySend` and `combine` block writing `currentRevisionId`) fixed by promoting the event to `data class BranchSwitchedEvent(val branchName: String)` carrying the user-supplied name from the source-of-truth event handler; LOW1 (`FakeChartBranchRepository.createBranch` idempotent return path unreachable from use case) addressed via in-code comment documenting the use-case pre-empt. Second-pass review APPROVED with zero findings. **Pre-push invariants all green**: `:shared:ktlintCheck`, `:shared:compileTestKotlinIosSimulatorArm64`, `:shared:testAndroidHostTest` (1033 tests), `:shared:koverVerify`, `bash scripts/verify-i18n-keys.sh` (301 keys). iOS build via `xcodegen generate && xcodebuild -project iosApp.xcodeproj -scheme iosApp -destination 'generic/platform=iOS Simulator' -configuration Debug build` ✅. **Closes Phase 37**: with this slice, the entire ADR-013 collaboration-core MVP — append-only history schema (37.1) → live history list (37.2) → side-by-side diff (37.3) → branch picker + restore (37.4) — is end-to-end functional. The "single-tip simplification" (only the checked-out branch's tip is materialized in `chart_documents` at any time) holds: switch branch reads the target's tip revision and rewrites the tip pointer atomically, the existing renderers are unchanged. **Scope cuts unchanged from ADR-013 §9**: no branch deletion UI yet (the `ChartBranchRepository.deleteBranch` method is wired but no caller surfaces it — defer until a real "I made too many branches" UX need shows up; the data layer is ready); no branch-from-arbitrary-revision affordance (ADR-013 §7 — branching from a past revision is the same shape as `RestoreRevisionUseCase` followed by branch-from-tip and adds picker complexity without a clear v1 use case); no Maestro E2E flow (linked-pattern + chart prerequisite same as Phase 32 / 37.3 deferral; reopen if real interaction-flow regressions surface). **Phase 38 forward-compat anchors hold**: `chart_revisions.author_id` is already provisioned for multi-author commits per 37.1; the owner-scoped `chart-revisions-<ownerId>` Realtime channel from 37.1 is the right shape for Phase 38's "watch upstream" subscription mechanism. Phase 38 (PR/merge) opens next.

- **Phase 38.4.1**: ChartViewer overflow → "Open pull request" entry (ADR-014 §6 — closes the only beta-blocking UX gap from 38.4 review). The data layer + `OpenPullRequestUseCase` shipped in 38.3, but the only way to actually invoke the open-PR flow before this slice was via ProjectDetail's PatternInfoSection on a forked pattern — most beta users would never discover it. **`ChartViewerViewModel` extension**: state gains `pattern: Pattern?`, `currentBranch: ChartBranch?`, `targetMainBranch: ChartBranch?`, `currentUserId: String?`, plus form-draft fields `openPrTitleDraft` / `openPrDescriptionDraft` / `pendingOpenPrSheet` / `isOpeningPullRequest` / `openPrError`. Derived gate `canOpenPullRequest` (state-class property, not top-level extension, so the Swift bridge reads it as a plain `Bool` getter — same precedent as `PullRequestDetailState.canMerge` / `canClose`). 6 new events: `RequestOpenPullRequest` (opens the form sheet, clears any prior error), `OpenPrTitleChanged(value)` / `OpenPrDescriptionChanged(value)` (form-draft updates), `ConfirmOpenPullRequest` (submit), `DismissOpenPullRequestSheet` (clears drafts + closes sheet — even mid-submission via SwiftUI swipe-to-dismiss), `ClearOpenPrError` (inline error dismiss). New sealed `ChartViewerNavEvent.PullRequestCreated(prId)` plus `Channel<ChartViewerNavEvent>(BUFFERED)` for one-shot post-submit navigation. Ctor gains 4 new nullable deps (`patternRepository` / `chartBranchRepository` / `authRepository` / `openPullRequest`) so existing test call-sites compile unchanged; production wiring through Koin uses `getOrNull()` so the gate gracefully degrades to closed in offline-only / mis-wired setups. **Branch resolution**: new `resolveOpenPrContext` private suspend fn fires from inside the chart-collect block; reads pattern + source branches + upstream's main branch with explicit try/catch + CancellationException rethrow per the Phase 36.3 / 37.x precedent. `lastResolvedRevisionId` local outside the collect block de-dups Realtime self-echoes that don't change the tip — same shape as `ProjectDetailViewModel.observeParentAttribution`'s Phase 36.5 `distinctUntilChanged` pattern. `resolveCurrentBranch` prefers an exact `tipRevisionId == chart.revisionId` match against the source pattern's branch list, falls back to the `"main"` branch by name when no exact match (the fallback keeps any "current branch" rendering helpful during cache lag). **Critical correctness fix from code review (MEDIUM-1)**: the `canOpenPullRequest` gate ALSO requires `branch.tipRevisionId == chart.revisionId` so the "main" fallback doesn't silently submit a PR with a (sourceBranchId, sourceTipRevisionId) pair that the merge RPC would immediately reject with "Source tip drifted" (which has no recovery path except closing and re-opening the PR once the cache catches up). Without the gate's exact-match check, a user on a feature branch with a "main" fallback would see the entry enabled and produce an immediately-unmergeable PR. **`openPullRequestInternal`**: gate snapshot at top + early-return if `isOpeningPullRequest`; resolves all required fields via `requireNotNull(...)` carrying explanatory messages naming the gate as the contract (HIGH fix from code review — `!!` violates project Kotlin coding-style rule); fallback when `openPullRequest` dep is null surfaces a hardcoded English `openPrError` consistent with the `PullRequestDetailViewModel.attemptMerge` offline-mode pattern + the Tech Debt Backlog ViewModel-error-localization deferral. Submit dispatches to the use case + on success emits `PullRequestCreated(prId)` and clears form drafts; on failure surfaces inline `openPrError` and keeps the sheet open for retry (deliberately separate from the top-level `errorMessage` field which displaces the chart with a centered Text — wrong UX for a form-submit failure). **Compose `ChartViewerScreen`**: overflow `DropdownMenuItem` "Open pull request" with `Icons.Default.Forum` icon — gated on `state.canOpenPullRequest` so non-fork patterns don't see the entry rather than rendering it disabled (keeps the menu length tight). New private `OpenPullRequestDialog` composable with `OutlinedTextField`s for title (singleLine, required) + description (minLines=3, optional), inline error rendering with `MaterialTheme.colorScheme.error`, confirm button enabled only when `!isSubmitting && titleDraft.isNotBlank()`. New `LaunchedEffect(viewModel)` collects `navEvents` → snackbars `message_pr_opened_successfully` + invokes `onOpenPullRequestNavigate(prId)` callback. testTags per ADR-014 §6 conventions: `openPullRequestMenuItem`, `openPullRequestDialog`, `openPrTitleInput`, `openPrDescriptionInput`, `openPrErrorLabel`, `confirmOpenPullRequestButton`. **NavGraph**: `composable<ChartViewer>` block plumbs `onOpenPullRequestNavigate = { prId -> navController.navigate(PullRequestDetail(prId = prId)) }` — same `PullRequestDetail` route already wired by Phase 38.3. **iOS mirror** at `iosApp/iosApp/Screens/StructuredChartViewerScreen.swift`: extended toolbar `Menu` with "Open pull request" Button (gated on `holder.state.canOpenPullRequest`) + `bubble.left.and.bubble.right` SF Symbol; `.sheet(isPresented: Binding<Bool>)` derived from `pendingOpenPrSheet` flag; new private `OpenPullRequestSheet` SwiftUI view (`NavigationStack` + `Form` with two `Section`s + Cancel/Open `ToolbarItem`s; title field uses `axis: .vertical` with `lineLimit(3...8)` for the description; confirm gated on `.disabled(isSubmitting || titleDraft.trimmingCharacters(in: .whitespacesAndNewlines).isEmpty)` matching Compose's `isNotBlank()` semantics). Toast for success uses the same 2-second `.overlay(alignment: .bottom)` pattern as the existing `switchedToast`; both toasts coexist via ZStack-style ordering with the `prOpenedToast` taking priority when both are non-nil. nav events Closeable observed in `.task` + closed in `.onDisappear` per the established Phase 32.2 / 36.5 iOS Closeable leak audit pattern; `.task` re-fires on view re-appearance so the helper closes any prior subscription before creating a new one. New iOS bridge `wrapChartViewerNavEvents` typed accessor in `KoinHelper.kt`. **i18n** — 7 new keys across all 5 sources (342 total, +7 from 335): `action_open_pull_request` (full-phrase overflow menu item, parallel to `action_pull_requests` toolbar entry), `dialog_open_pull_request_title`, `label_pr_title` (parallel to existing `label_pr_description` from 38.3), `hint_pr_title` (with U+2026 ellipsis per Phase 33.1.3 placeholder convention), `hint_pr_description_optional`, `action_open_pr` (short-form dialog confirm button — parallel to `action_close_pr` / `action_merge_pr` from 38.3 / 38.4), `message_pr_opened_successfully`. JA semantically diverges with 「プルリクエストを作成」("create") over the literal「開く」per the GitHub JA UI convention; documented inline in the JA strings comment block. Reuses `action_cancel`, `label_pr_description`, `title_error`, `action_ok`. **Tests (+11 commonTest, 1166 → 1177)**: 11 new `ChartViewerViewModelTest` cases covering canOpenPullRequest gate true/false on fork/non-fork/non-owner/missing-target-main, the MEDIUM-1 regression anchor (`currentBranch falls back to main but PR-open gate stays closed when tip does not match chart`), draft updates, RequestOpen clears prior error + opens sheet, Dismiss clears drafts, ConfirmOpen happy path emits PullRequestCreated and writes correct branch/pattern ids through to the use case, ConfirmOpen failure surfaces openPrError without closing sheet, ConfirmOpen no-op when gate is closed. Plus a private `ForkChartRevisionFake` helper for the OpenPullRequestUseCase parent-chain walk (the algorithm itself is exercised in `OpenPullRequestUseCaseTest`'s 9 tests; this fake just makes the source tip the common ancestor on the first hop). New `OpenPrTestRig` data class + `makeOpenPrViewModel(...)` parametric helper for arrange-phase setup. Test names follow the Phase 32 Kotlin/Native CI gotcha (no parens, commas, or apostrophes in backticks). **Code review**: 0 CRITICAL / 1 HIGH / 1 MEDIUM / 2 LOW first pass — all 4 fixed pre-commit. **HIGH** (5 `!!` operators in `openPullRequestInternal` violate project Kotlin coding-style rule "Never use `!!` — prefer `requireNotNull()` / `checkNotNull()`") fixed by replacing all with `requireNotNull(current.X) { "canOpenPullRequest gate: X is null" }` carrying gate-naming messages. **MEDIUM-1** (gate fallback to "main" can silently submit PR with mismatched sourceBranchId/sourceTipRevisionId on a feature branch — would land an immediately unmergeable PR rejected by the merge RPC's `chart_branches.tip_revision_id == sourceTipRevisionId` validation) fixed by tightening the `canOpenPullRequest` gate to require `branch.tipRevisionId == c.revisionId` exact match; the fallback in `resolveCurrentBranch` stays for displayed-branch rendering but the gate guards correctness. **LOW-1** (offline-mode error string hardcoded English) acknowledged consistent with existing PullRequestDetailViewModel.attemptMerge precedent + Tech Debt Backlog deferral; documented inline. **LOW-2** (`resolveOpenPrContext` fires redundantly on every Realtime echo) fixed via `lastResolvedRevisionId` de-dup local. Second-pass review APPROVED with one new doc-only LOW (the `resolveOpenPrContext` KDoc said "re-runs on every chart emission" but the code now de-dups; updated KDoc to accurately describe the de-dup semantics + name the parallel to `ProjectDetailViewModel.observeParentAttribution`). **Pre-push invariants all green**: `:shared:ktlintCheck`, `:shared:compileTestKotlinIosSimulatorArm64`, `:shared:testAndroidHostTest` (1177 tests, +11 from 1166 baseline), `:shared:koverVerify`, `bash scripts/verify-i18n-keys.sh` (342 keys). iOS app builds via `xcodebuild -project iosApp.xcodeproj -scheme iosApp -destination 'generic/platform=iOS Simulator' -configuration Debug build` ✅. **Scope cuts unchanged from Phase 38.4 review**: three-pane canvas preview on `ChartConflictResolutionScreen` (DualCanvasPanel extraction is meaningful refactor); Maestro E2E flow for the open-PR happy path (linked-pattern + chart-divergence fixture overhead with no clear value gain over the 11 new ViewModel tests + 9 use-case tests — reopen if real interaction-flow regressions surface); iOS toast for the chart-clone failure path on Discovery (Phase 36.5+ polish). **Closes the open-PR entry-point gap that 38.4 review flagged as the only beta-blocking UX issue**; the entire ADR-014 collaboration loop is now reachable end-to-end from any forked pattern's chart viewer. Phase 39 (Closed Beta) prep is the natural next slice now that the loop is observable to real users.

- **Phase 38.4**: Merge + conflict resolution (ADR-014 §4 §5 §6 §8) — fourth and final code slice of Phase 38, closes the entire collaboration loop. **`ConflictDetector` algorithm** under `domain/chart/ConflictDetector.kt` per ADR-014 §4 — pure 3-way wrapper over the existing Phase 37 `ChartDiffAlgorithm`. Computes `diff(ancestor, theirs)` and `diff(ancestor, mine)` then per-cell-coordinate partitions changes into `autoFromTheirs` / `autoFromMine` / `conflicts` based on whether both sides changed the same `(layerId, x, y)`. Same shape applies at the layer level (`autoLayerFromTheirs` / `autoLayerFromMine` / `layerConflicts`). Both-sides-agree-on-same-target case auto-resolves to autoFromTheirs (either side renders identically). Polar charts handled identically — `(x, y)` keys are `(stitch, ring)`. Returns `ConflictReport(autoFromTheirs, autoFromMine, conflicts, autoLayerFromTheirs, autoLayerFromMine, layerConflicts)` with `isClean: Boolean = conflicts.isEmpty() && layerConflicts.isEmpty()`. `CellConflict` and `LayerConflict` data classes carry `id: String` derived properties (`"$layerId#$x,$y"` / `layerId`) for SwiftUI ForEach `id: \.id` consistency with the Phase 38.3 PR list / comment ForEach precedent. **`MergePullRequestUseCase`** invokes the SECURITY DEFINER `merge_pull_request` RPC per ADR-014 §5. Bypasses the standard local-then-sync orchestration since the RPC is the only writer permitted to produce `chart_revisions.author_id != owner_id` rows. Defense-in-depth precondition gates: status must be OPEN, caller must be signed in, caller must be target owner per `PatternRepository.getById(targetPatternId)?.ownerId == callerId` (the RPC's `WHERE owner_id = v_caller` is the actual security boundary; the use-case check just surfaces a clear "Only the target owner can merge" Validation error rather than letting the RPC RAISE bubble up as Unknown). Mints fresh `revisionId` per call (Uuid.random) so PendingSync retry semantics are idempotent. Encodes `resolvedChart.toDocumentJson()` as the JSONB document parameter; computes a fresh `contentHash` via `StructuredChart.computeContentHash` over `extents + layers`. Maps RPC `RAISE EXCEPTION` messages onto distinct `UseCaseError` subtypes via `mapMergeError` — "Source tip drifted" / "PR not open" / "Target branch has no tip" → Validation, "Caller is not target owner" → Authentication, "PR not found" → NotFound, anything unrecognized → `Exception.toUseCaseError()` Unknown. Returns `MergeResult(pullRequestId, mergedRevisionId, mergedContentHash)` envelope on success. Standard `try { ... } catch (e: CancellationException) { throw e } catch (e: Exception) { ... }` envelope per the Phase 36.3 / 37.x precedent. **Merge port abstraction** (`domain/repository/PullRequestMergeOperations.kt`): thin `interface PullRequestMergeOperations { suspend fun merge(...): String }` that `RemotePullRequestDataSource` implements via `supabaseClient.postgrest.rpc("merge_pull_request", params)`. Same ports-and-adapters layering as `ChartRevisionRepository` / `StructuredChartRepository` — domain layer defines the contract, data layer provides the Supabase-typed adapter. Tests inject an in-memory fake without standing up Supabase. **`applyResolutions` helper** (in `MergePullRequestUseCase.kt`): pure function that builds the resolved drawing payload by starting from `mine` (target tip), applying `autoLayerFromTheirs` first (so subsequent cell ops see the correct layer set), then `layerConflictPicks`, then `autoFromTheirs`, then per-conflict `cellResolutions`. SKIP picks the ancestor cell value (revert to pre-fork state); KEEP_MINE / TAKE_THEIRS pick from the respective side. **Critical correctness fix from code review**: HIGH-2 caught that a SKIP cell pick on a layer that was auto-removed by theirs would silently recreate an orphan cell bucket via `cellsByLayerXy.getOrPut(coord.layerId) { mutableMapOf() }` — but the final `mergedLayers` build only iterates `layersById.values`, so the cell would silently disappear. Fix: `if (!layersById.containsKey(coord.layerId)) continue` skips the pick entirely when the containing layer is gone. Similar reasoning for KEEP_MINE on a removed layer — the user's only chance to preserve the layer was the (non-existent) layer-conflict pick at the layer level; cell-level KEEP_MINE cannot resurrect the layer. Recomputes rect chart extents from the merged cells; polar charts preserve their structural extents. **`ChartConflictResolutionViewModel`** parameterized on `prId`. Loads ancestor / theirs / mine snapshots in `init` (revisions are immutable per ADR-013 §1, no Flow observation), runs `ConflictDetector.detect`, exposes per-conflict picker state. `canApplyAndMerge` derived gate flips true only when every cell + layer conflict has a resolution. ApplyAndMerge dispatches `applyResolutions` over the user's picks and routes the result through `MergePullRequestUseCase`. Emits `ChartConflictResolutionNavEvent.MergeApplied(mergedRevisionId)` on success. **`PullRequestDetailViewModel.attemptMerge`** (new method, replaces the inert merge confirmation): when user confirms the merge dialog, loads ancestor + theirs + mine, runs `ConflictDetector.detect`, and either (a) routes through `MergePullRequestUseCase` directly with `applyResolutions(mine, autoFromTheirs, emptyMap(), autoLayerFromTheirs, emptyMap(), theirs, ancestor)` for the auto-clean path (HIGH-1 fix from code review — passing `theirs` raw silently dropped target-side `autoFromMine` edits because `autoFromMine` is identity-over-mine, so we still need to apply autoFromTheirs ON mine, not start from theirs), or (b) emits `NavigateToConflictResolution(prId)` for the conflicts path. New nav events `PrMerged(mergedRevisionId)` + `NavigateToConflictResolution(prId)` join the existing `PrClosed`. ViewModel ctor gains optional nullable `MergePullRequestUseCase` / `ChartRevisionRepository` / `StructuredChartRepository` deps with default-null so existing tests stay valid; production wiring always provides non-null; `attemptMerge` surfaces a Validation error if any are missing. New `isMerging` field added to `PullRequestDetailState`. **Compose `ChartConflictResolutionScreen`**: Scaffold + TopAppBar with summary chip ("3 conflicts to resolve" parametric). Phone-first stack — three-pane canvas (ancestor pinned center, theirs/mine side-by-side) named in ADR-014 §6 deferred to a polish slice (same scope-cut precedent as Phase 36.4 iOS Discovery thumbnail; row-based picker UI alone closes the merge loop end-to-end and the canvas preview can land independently). LazyColumn renders `LayerConflictRow` (uses `conflict.theirs?.name ?: mine?.name ?: ancestor?.name` for the human-readable layer name — code review MEDIUM-2 fix; the prior version rendered the bare UUID as the user-visible label) + `CellConflictRow` (parametric `label_conflict_cell` "Cell (%1$d, %2$d)"). Each row shows a 3-button `ResolutionPickerRow` (Take theirs / Keep mine / Skip) — selected option uses `Button` (filled), unselected use `TextButton` (outlined).
