- **Phase 39.0.1**: Pre-launch infrastructure (2026-04-27 single-session sweep) — Supabase prod backfill + branch protection + self-hosted CI + security hardening, all completed before tester invites go out. (1) **Supabase prod schema migration** ([commit 80f00fb](https://github.com/b150005/knit-note/commit/80f00fb)): prod was 7 migrations behind (009 pattern_metadata / 010 progress_photos / 011 visibility_index / 013 project_segments / 014 pattern_attribution / 015 chart_revisions / 016 pull_requests). Resolved local-vs-remote 012_structured_chart version mismatch via `supabase migration repair --status reverted 20260417114618` + `--status applied 012`, then `supabase db push --include-all`. Migration 010 hit `operator does not exist: uuid = text` on the shared-progress-photos RLS policy (the JOIN compared `shares.pattern_id` UUID with `projects.pattern_id` TEXT — Phase 1 legacy schema mismatch). Patched the local file with `s.pattern_id::text` cast and applied the missing statements (bucket + 5 policies + ALTER TABLE activities CHECK) directly via `mcp__supabase__execute_sql`. All 16 migrations now match across local + prod. Closes Phase 39 Gate 1. (2) **Branch protection ruleset** ([commit 9054ea2](https://github.com/b150005/knit-note/commit/9054ea2), ruleset id `15581036`): `main-strict` ruleset with 6 rules (`update`, `non_fast_forward`, `deletion`, `required_linear_history`, `pull_request` requiring 1 approval + dismiss-stale + require-last-push-approval + require-thread-resolution, `required_status_checks` for 6 contexts). Bypass actor: Repository Admin role only — on a personal-account repo, this means Owner-only by default. `docs/en/repo-policy.md` + JA mirror documents the design + rationale; CLAUDE.md `## Development Workflow` section references it. Verified by attempting direct push: server returns "Bypassed rule violations" + "6 of 6 required status checks are expected" message confirming the rules are active. (3) **Self-hosted GHA runner pivot** ([commits 92fa802 → 1a119e1](https://github.com/b150005/knit-note/compare/92fa802...1a119e1)): originally provisioned a Lume macOS 26.4.1 VM (CPU 4 / RAM 8GB / disk 100GB) via `lume create --unattended tahoe`, manually completed Setup Assistant via VNC after the preset-driven setup hit `Text 'Set Up Later' not found`, installed Homebrew + xcodes + gh + JDK 17 + xcodegen + Maestro, manually installed Xcode 26.4.1 via `xcodes install` (Apple Developer 2FA prompts that env-var-passed app-specific password could not bypass), downloaded iOS 26.4 Simulator runtime, registered GHA runner as `lume-vm-1` with LaunchAgent. **Then pivoted to host-direct runner** because the threat model audit (see point 4 below) found the VM isolation provided minimal security delta given strict-ruleset restricts main pushes to Owner only and `pull_request` workflow trigger is blocked by GitHub's "Require approval for all outside collaborators" setting — meanwhile the VM added 70GB disk + Setup Assistant friction + duplicate Xcode/SDK + slower builds. Deregistered VM runner, deleted VM, installed runner binary at `/Users/b150005/Development/Tools/actions-runner-knitnote/` registered as `b150005mac-host` with labels `[self-hosted, macos, apple-silicon, host]`. All workflows migrated to single sequential self-hosted runner: `ci.yml` (3 jobs) + `e2e.yml` (2 jobs) + `security.yml` (matrix 2) + `pages.yml`. Per-job optimizations: dropped `actions/setup-java@v5` (use host JDK 17 via `JAVA_HOME` env), reused host Xcode + Simulator + Android SDK + Maestro + xcodegen (zero per-runner DL after first run). Per-job cleanup step deletes workspace `build/` folders + `~/Library/Developer/Xcode/DerivedData/iosApp-*` + Maestro test results (preserves `~/.gradle/caches/`, Android SDK, Xcode, user's other simulators). Android E2E `arch: x86_64 → arm64-v8a` for native HVF speed; `enable-kvm` Linux-only step removed. Deleted unused `ios-self-hosted.yml` (consolidated into ci.yml ios job) + `ci-base.yml` (ECC base template leftover). `release.yml` kept on GitHub-hosted (TestFlight signing complexity, tag-only trigger). First post-pivot CI run on host: `ci.yml ios` job completed in 6m18s (vs ~25min on macos-latest, 4× faster). Single-runner sequential trade-off: total cycle ~80min vs ~25min parallel — accepted for solo-dev simplicity per user choice. **Android E2E runtime gotcha**: host AVD persists across CI runs and across local-dev sessions, so a prior dev install of `io.github.b150005.knitnote.android` signed with user's local debug keystore conflicts with CI's default debug keystore — `INSTALL_FAILED_UPDATE_INCOMPATIBLE`. Fixed in [commit 7a9101b](https://github.com/b150005/knit-note/commit/7a9101b) by adding `adb uninstall io.github.b150005.knitnote.android || true` before the `adb install -r` step. (4) **Security hardening per audit** ([commit 8d6c6ae](https://github.com/b150005/knit-note/commit/8d6c6ae)): security-reviewer agent audit found 2 CRITICAL + 4 HIGH + 2 MEDIUM + 2 LOW. **CRITICAL C1** (public repo + self-hosted + `pull_request` trigger = arbitrary code execution by any GitHub user) closed by setting Repository Settings → Actions → "Fork pull request workflows from outside collaborators" → "Require approval for all outside collaborators" (was previously "Require approval for first-time contributors who are new to GitHub" which still allowed code execution from established GitHub users). **CRITICAL C2** (third-party action supply chain via mutable tag re-pointing) closed by SHA-pinning `reactivecircus/android-emulator-runner@v2` → `@e89f39f`, `gradle/actions/setup-gradle@v6` → `@50e97c2`, `softprops/action-gh-release@v3` → `@b430933`. Dependabot tracks the SHAs via existing `.github/dependabot.yml` `github-actions` ecosystem. **HIGH H3** (`ci.yml` lacked top-level `permissions:` block — silent inheritance of repo default) closed by explicit `permissions: contents: read` matching `e2e.yml` posture. **HIGH H4** (overzealous "全部 self-hosted" included `pages.yml` whose `id-token: write` permission should not exist in host process space) closed by reverting `pages.yml` to `runs-on: ubuntu-latest` (the static-file Pages deploy has no Apple Silicon dependency anyway). **MEDIUM M1** (`${{ steps.sim.outputs.dest }}` interpolated directly into shell — structurally vulnerable even though current value is system-controlled) closed by env-var-then-shell-var pattern: `env: XCODE_DEST: ${{ steps.sim.outputs.dest }}` then `xcodebuild ... -destination "$XCODE_DEST"`. **LOW L1** (`pages.yml` `actions/checkout@v4` while everywhere else is `@v6`) closed by version bump. Verified Repository Settings → "Secret scanning" + "Push protection" both ENABLED. Outstanding (post-beta, intentionally deferred): **HIGH H1** persistent workspace cross-run poisoning + **HIGH H2** runner runs as admin-group user with full Keychain access + **MEDIUM M2** shared `~/.gradle/caches/` between CI and local dev (all three would require runner isolation via Lume VM revival or similar — significant work, threat model accepts the residual risk for solo-maintainer with strict-ruleset main + fork PR approval gate); **LOW L2** unrestricted runner network egress (would require 3rd-party macOS firewall like Little Snitch); **user-side action item** Dependabot security updates not yet enabled (Settings → Code security & analysis); **user-side action item** `~/.ssh/id_ed25519` + `~/.ssh/b150005-GitHub` lack passphrase (advised `ssh-keygen -p` post-beta when convenient — silent exfiltration risk if runner ever compromised). All findings + mitigations + deferred items documented in `docs/en/repo-policy.md`'s Security section ([commit included]). **CodeQL Kotlin status update** (CLAUDE.md "CI Known Limitations" updated in same commit): the Kotlin 2.3.20-not-supported entry was outdated as of 2026-04-15 when CodeQL CLI 2.25.2 added Kotlin 2.3.20 support. The Security workflow's java-kotlin matrix entry continues to fail but with a different error: `CodeQL detected code written in Java/Kotlin but this run didn't build any of it` — root cause now is the CodeQL Kotlin extractor failing to capture the Gradle in-process compilation despite the documented `--no-daemon` + `kotlin.daemon.enabled=false` + `kotlin.compiler.execution.strategy=in-process` flags. Reproduces identically on host runner so not runner-specific. `continue-on-error: true` keeps the job from blocking CI; `required_status_checks` excludes this matrix entry. Investigation deferred. No code/test delta in this slice (infrastructure + docs only). (5) **Reverted self-hosted runner back to GitHub-hosted** (commit, single batch reverting `ci.yml` + `e2e.yml` + `security.yml` `runs-on:` from `[self-hosted, macos, apple-silicon, host]` to `ubuntu-latest` / `macos-latest`). Reasoning: even after closing CRITICAL C1 + C2 from the security audit, the host-runner setup carried two material problems: (a) **inherent residual security risk on a public repo** — H1 (persistent workspace cross-run poisoning) + H2 (admin-user keychain access) cannot be closed without runner isolation (Lume VM revival or equivalent), and the deferred items list was uncomfortable to ship with closed-beta tester invites going out; and (b) **host-PC operational overhead** — observed real failures during shakedown: CI `:shared:build` step hit `Gradle build daemon stopped: JVM GC thrashing` despite `GRADLE_OPTS=-Xmx6g` (commit `24194b9`), iOS E2E `xcrun simctl install` hung for 42 minutes before the 45-min timeout killed the job (host's iPhone 17 Pro Simulator carried a dev install of knit-note), Android E2E earlier hit `INSTALL_FAILED_UPDATE_INCOMPATIBLE` for the same reason on the host's persistent AVD (commit `7a9101b` adb uninstall fix). Each fix accreted complexity, and the host runner kept surfacing new state-persistence problems that GitHub-hosted ephemeral runners structurally do not have. Net cost-benefit: 4× iOS speedup (6m18s vs 25min on macos-latest) and ~$0/month CI cost vs. ongoing host maintenance burden + security exposure on a public repo + recurring user-side AVD/Simulator hygiene. Reverted to GitHub-hosted, **kept all security hardening that's still applicable**: SHA-pin third-party actions (still valid, supply chain risk applies regardless of runner), `permissions: contents: read` on ci.yml (defense in depth), env-var pattern for `${{ steps.sim.outputs.dest }}` (M1 fix is structurally correct), `pages.yml` on ubuntu-latest (was the right call from H4), `actions/checkout@v6` unification, `security.yml` concurrency block (queue management, applies to GitHub-hosted too), GHA "Fork pull request workflows from outside collaborators" set to "Require approval for all outside collaborators" (defense for any future self-hosted experiment + general OSS hygiene), Dependabot security updates enabled. Stopped LaunchAgent + uninstalled service + deregistered runner via `gh api -X DELETE /repos/b150005/knit-note/actions/runners/22` + deleted `/Users/b150005/Development/Tools/actions-runner-knitnote/` directory. `docs/en/repo-policy.md` "Security posture (self-hosted CI runner)" section deleted (no longer accurate; the branch protection ruleset section remains). Lume CLI itself stays installed on host for any future ad-hoc VM use, but no longer integrated with GHA. Net effect on Phase 39 launch: CI returns to the parallel-on-3-runners GitHub-hosted model (~25min total per push), all 6 required status checks (`Shared Module`, `Android (Build + Test)`, `iOS (Build + Test)`, `Android E2E (Maestro)`, `iOS E2E (Maestro)`, `CodeQL Analysis (swift, macos-latest, manual)`) targeting the canonical hosted runner labels they were originally written for. Lesson learned recorded for future readers: self-hosted on a public repo demands isolation (VM/container) — the apparent speedup from running on real hardware is offset by the security and maintenance burden, and ephemeral GitHub-hosted runners' fresh-state guarantee is more valuable than it looks.

- **i18n sweep across remaining shared screens** (**CLOSED as of Phase 33.1.15** — left here as historical trail; zero shared Compose surfaces remain that hardcode English. also caught a latent HIGH in `iosAppUITests/OnboardingUITests.swift` where `app.staticTexts["English title"]` queries would break on Japanese-locale simulators — migrated to `app.otherElements["onboardingPage1..3"]` via `.accessibilityIdentifier`), Phase 33.1.5 migrated `LoginScreen` (+ established the `action_*` vs `label_*` precedent for interactive button labels per code-review MEDIUM1 — toggle-mode buttons are `action_toggle_to_*` not `label_toggle_to_*`; documented `title_error` for single-button error alerts in the convention; followed-up MEDIUM3 deferred — net-new `LoginUITests.swift` to write alongside Maestro Login flows when Supabase is exercised end-to-end), Phase 33.1.6 migrated `ProfileScreen` (+ introduced the `message_*` role prefix for transient action-completion feedback like Snackbar/Toast; added the SwiftUI literal-promotion table to the convention doc distinguishing auto-localizing APIs like `Text("key")` from overload-ambiguous ones like `.alert("key", ...)`; established that SwiftUI state-branch containers need a concrete layout node like `ZStack` — a bare `Group` is layout-transparent and propagates accessibility modifiers to each child branch independently, breaking the landmark query), Phase 33.1.7 migrated `ActivityFeedScreen` (+ parametric activity templates with `%1$s` / `%1$@` substitution preserving Japanese `{name}が{verb}` grammar, and unified the author-lookup fallback on `label_someone` across platforms — Android was incorrectly rendering "You"), Phase 33.1.8 migrated `SettingsScreen` (+ established platform-idiom divergence is acceptable for dialog confirm-button wording — Compose `AlertDialog` uses short "Delete" and iOS `.confirmationDialog` uses full "Delete Account"; also codified extending the `.confirmationDialog` "needs explicit `LocalizedStringKey` wrap" rule to its `message:` closure content, not just the outer title parameter), Phase 33.1.9 migrated `DiscoveryScreen` (+ codified the empty-state-body key-convention as `state_*_body` suffix to match the established `state_no_projects_body` / `state_no_matching_projects_body` siblings; established that `.navigationTitle` on non-conditional literals should still wrap explicitly with `LocalizedStringKey(...)` for consistency with all preceding 33.1.x migrations, even though the convention-doc literal-promotion table says a bare literal would work — consistency wins; introduced `label_difficulty_*` as a distinct domain prefix from `label_status_*` because they are different filter taxonomies; per-chip testTag landmarks `difficulty{All,Beginner,Intermediate,Advanced}Chip` established as the pattern for multi-chip filter bars that will otherwise have locale-dependent Maestro taps), and Phase 33.1.10 migrated `PatternLibraryScreen` (+ promoted `Difficulty.labelKey` from `DiscoveryScreen.kt` private to `ui/components/DifficultyLabels.kt` public shared extension — first shared i18n helper extension in the codebase; established the precedent that when a second screen needs the same enum→StringResource mapping, promote to `ui/components/` and add an exhaustive test rather than duplicate the `when` block; also harmonized iOS and Android delete-confirmation wording by switching iOS from a generic short body to a parametric `dialog_delete_pattern_body` via `String(format: NSLocalizedString(...), pendingDeleteName)`), and Phase 33.1.13 migrated `SharedContentScreen` (+ established that an iOS-only key still shipping in all 5 i18n sources for `verify-i18n-keys.sh` parity needs an explicit intent comment in the shared EN strings file so future readers don't assume symmetric Android usage — see `state_could_not_load`; also established that JA translations semantically diverging from bare-literal EN — `プロジェクト数` vs `Projects` — should carry a comment in the JA strings file when the divergence is intentional for contextual clarity rather than a translator judgement call; also established that `default` branches in Swift enum switches forced by Kotlin→ObjC bridging should return a locale-neutral non-empty fallback like `enum.name` rather than empty string so future Kotlin enum additions without matching Swift updates surface visibly rather than as blank UI cells), and Phase 33.1.14 migrated `SharedWithMeScreen` (+ established that platform-idiom divergence for a list-row render style — Android single pipe-separated line vs iOS bullet-separated HStack fragments — is acceptable only if **both platforms consume the same parametric keys**; a code reviewer caught iOS silently dropping the "From"/"Shared on" prefixes because `Text(verbatim: sharerName)` rendered the bare value and the parametric keys defined in xcstrings went unused — generalizable lesson is that "iOS renders fragments visually" does not permit skipping the parametric keys; route through `String(format: NSLocalizedString("key", comment: ""), arg)` so translators see the full sentence context and future platform re-renders stay consistent; also bundled two pre-existing Android bugs as i18n-adjacent fixes — the raw enum name render `share.permission.name` → "VIEW"/"FORK" uppercase and the sharer-null branch that omitted the "From" prefix entirely — both harmonized via `label_someone` fallback and `label_permission_{view,fork}`; `label_share_status_*` established as a distinct domain prefix from `label_status_*` since share status and project status are separate taxonomies). The following shared Compose screens still hardcode English and need the same `stringResource(Res.string.*)` treatment: `CommentSection` (1 explicitly enumerated after 33.1.14). Also deferred from 33.1.12 scope: `UserPickerDialog.kt` (Android-only, triggered from ProjectDetailScreen toolbar "Share with user" IconButton — contentDescription is migrated but the dialog body itself is not). Each migration adds its own domain keys to all 5 i18n sources and should be cut as its own PR. **Note for Maestro flows**: once a screen's title becomes i18n'd, any existing `assertVisible: "<English title>"` must be replaced with the screen's stable testTag (as done for `P1_symbol_gallery.yaml` and the `onboardingPage{1,2,3}` testTags in 33.1.4) — otherwise the flow fails the moment CMP resolves to the Japanese locale or the (now-asynchronous) resource takes a beat to load. Same rule applies to **iOS XCUITests**: any `app.staticTexts["literal"]` query against i18n'd copy must pivot to `app.otherElements["testTag"]` (33.1.4 caught this on Onboarding). Also: Maestro `tapOn: "text"` uses regex; literal `...` matches 3 chars but Unicode `\u2026` (`…`) is 1 char — any U+2026 ellipsis introduction (common for placeholders per the `state_loading` style) must either update the flow's regex or route through a testTag.
- **Maestro `text: "Back"` / `text: "Clear search"` brittleness** (**CLOSED as of Phase 33.4** — left here as historical trail; both halves are resolved. Non-dialog sites: Phase 33.2 pivoted all 12 shared screens to `backButton` / `clearSearchButton` / `editProjectButton` / `filter*Chip` testTags. Dialog-content sites: Phase 33.4 landed the `expect/actual` `Modifier.dialogTestTagsAsResourceId()` helper (path (b) — invasive Compose workaround from the 33.2 open-question list) that applies `.semantics { testTagsAsResourceId = true }` inside the AlertDialog window itself, bypassing the root Box's inability to propagate through the window boundary. All 9 Android Maestro flows now use `id:` selectors for dialog content (`newProjectDialog`, `editProjectDialog`, `projectNameInput`, `totalRowsInput`, `createProjectButton`, `saveButton`). Verified on both en-US (8/8 ✅) and ja-JP (8/8 ✅) Android emulator runs — the ja-JP pass is now locale-independent and no longer load-bearing on the dialogs staying English-hardcoded. Two holdout iOS nav-title text assertions (`assertVisible: "New Project"` / `"Edit Project"`) remain because SwiftUI `NavigationStack` title is not an `accessibilityIdentifier`-addressable element; documented with inline comments pointing at the pending iOS ProjectList i18n sweep.)
- **ViewModel error-message localization**: `errorMessage: String?` fields on ViewModels are displayed raw to the user — if a ViewModel populates them from a Kotlin exception, Japanese users see English. Need a typed error channel (`UseCaseError` → `StringResource`) rather than free-form strings. Deferred per Phase 33 non-goals; reopen after the shared-screen i18n sweep completes.
- **Maestro E2E for chart editor**: deferred because the "Edit structured chart" entry is gated on `state.pattern != null` (Project → Pattern linkage). Flow needs a pattern-create pre-step (~60 LOC). Reopening depends on E2E value vs. the 17-case ViewModel test coverage.
- **Android per-app locale non-functional** (**CLOSED in Phase 33.3** — left here as historical trail; `androidApp/build.gradle.kts` now opts into `generateLocaleConfig = true` with `localeFilters += listOf("en", "ja")` and `androidApp/src/main/res/resources.properties` declares `unqualifiedResLocale=en-US`. AGP generates `xml/_generated_res_locale_config.xml` and auto-injects `android:localeConfig` into the merged manifest. Android Settings > App Info > Language picker works end-to-end on Android 13+; ja-JP Maestro run 8/8 ✅.): historical context — Android 13+'s `LocaleManagerService` stored per-app locale values when set via `adb shell cmd locale set-app-locales <pkg> --locales ja-JP` but the runtime `Activity.Configuration.getLocales()` did not honor them, so CMP's `Res.string.*` and Android-native `R.string.*` both resolved to the system locale regardless of the user's selection. Discovered during Phase 33.2-verify; resolved in Phase 33.3. See the Phase 33.3 Completed entry for the `localeFilters` aapt2-vs-BCP-47 format gotcha captured as a Gradle inline comment.

### KMP / Compose recurring gotchas
- **Kotlin/Native test-name restriction**: backticked function names containing `(`, `)`, `,` fail `:shared:compileTestKotlinIosSimulatorArm64` / `IosX64` but pass `:shared:testAndroidHostTest` (JVM). Hit Phase 32 CI once (commit 6b65df4 is the fix). Pre-push verification should include the iOS simulator compile target; consider adding to `docs/en/` or a pre-push hook.
- **ktlint multiline formatting**: multiline expressions (e.g. `hasUnsavedChanges = computeUnsavedChanges(...)` with wrapped args) must start the call on a new line. JVM builds tolerate the inline form; CI `ktlintCommonMainSourceSetCheck` rejects it. Pre-push verification should include `./gradlew ktlintCheck` (or at minimum run `ktlintFormat` before committing). Hit Phase 32.2 CI once (commit 739fc82 is the fix).
- **`BackHandler` not in commonMain**: `androidx.activity.compose.BackHandler` cannot be used directly from shared Compose screens. Resolved in Phase 32.4 by adding `ui/platform/SystemBackHandler.kt` (`expect/actual`). Use `SystemBackHandler(enabled, onBack)` from any shared screen that needs to intercept Android system-back. iOS actual is a no-op (iOS uses SwiftUI screens, not shared Compose).

### Deprecated-API cleanup (low priority)
- `rememberSwipeToDismissBoxState` — 3 screens (PatternLibrary, ProjectDetail, ProjectList). No non-experimental CMP 1.10.3 replacement yet.
- `MenuAnchorType` typealias in CreateProjectDialog — rename to `ExposedDropdownMenuAnchorType`.
- `AuthRepositoryImpl.RefreshFailureCause` — migrate to `AuthEvent.RefreshFailure(cause)` per supabase-kt API change.

### Structured chart cosmetic polish
- `jis.crochet.reverse-sc` chevron form — awaiting real-user feedback before changing.

### Discovery (Phase 36 follow-ups)
- **iOS Discovery thumbnail live-render** (Phase 36.4 deferred to Phase 36.4.1): the Compose `ChartThumbnail` composable in `shared/.../ui/chart/ChartThumbnail.kt` renders a live mini-chart by reusing the public `drawSymbolPath` / `drawPolarGrid` / `drawPolarCells` helpers. iOS currently ships a static `Image(systemName: "square.grid.3x3.fill")` placeholder thumbnail that taps through to the read-only chart viewer — same routing, different rendering fidelity. Mirroring the live render on iOS requires factoring `iosApp/.../StructuredChartViewerScreen.swift`'s private `ChartCanvasView` struct out of its gestural host (it is ~200 LOC tightly bound with segment overlay, transform gestures, and tap dispatching) into a thumbnail-friendly variant. The data layer (`state.patternsWithCharts` companion set) is already at platform parity, so the only iOS gap is rendering. Same scope-cut pattern as Phase 36.3's iOS chart-clone-failure toast deferral: ship the data layer + Compose UI + iOS placeholder/route on the data slice, polish the iOS rendering on a follow-up.

### Future opportunistic crochet catalog additions (post-30.4)
- Foundation stitches (`fsc`, `fdc`) — US-dominant convention; defer until a JP-pattern user reports needing them.
- Extended sc (`exsc`) — CYC-standard, JIS silent.
- Spike stitches (long-loop variants) — colorwork crochet.
- `turning-ch-N` family — ADR-009 §9 open question (parametric vs. discrete family); reopens when a concrete non-dc-height turning chain shows up in a user pattern.
